When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by any methods; and you see the patient suffering badly and with great virtue, if make one great cautery on the stomach according to what is spoken here before or the cautery of the stomach, to the circulatory cautery; and three subtle cauterizations around the mouth, each a small, subtle cautery, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each toe, and two small cauterizations on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and they are ancient and consist of gross, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, but it does not profit, if make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely under the almecdate pome and pome in triangling, and one cautery under the mouth. Two others;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is chilled and the meat is not cooked, and one sees the face inflamed, then make one great cautery on the stomach, as said before, and one other on the liver, and one other on the kidneys at all the subtle cauterizations; and leave the cautery open for a long time. After that, cure the limb until it is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thelul, if it seems like a razor, then put the cautery all ablaze on that thelul cut; and I leave it for as long as the cauterizations come to the beginning of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after that, cure with ointments that are beneficial until they are sound; and if you make a great cautery on the alchatim, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an ill-cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure surgery or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes such a disease that it cannot be healed unless by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to anyone, and is inflamed and discharges putrid matter and corrupt moistures, then you must prove the entire tent very subtle, and take care that you know exactly how deep it is. After that, sharpen the cautery which seems like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity of the tent that has entered it, and continue the cautery until the corrupted flesh and matter are burned away, once or twice or three times, according to the necessity of the case; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the great veins. If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestine, then beware of those places, and do not make fires except in a charred place, and think that it is not yet purged; after that, cure the limb until it is sound, and if the limb is seared, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the limb is entirely sound; and if the matter is not removed, know that the limb is tormented, and the bone is corrupted at its foundation; and thus as one of those things which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and great windiness, and does not take a feminine shape, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other at the subtle cautery that we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will bring greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part in front of the bladder, where the hair of the wrist begins, and one to the right and one to the left, and each of them be as long as the length of a finger; and make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauterizations be subtle according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not allow conception to occur, and the flowers are corrupted and their terminations are late; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that three cauterizations be made around the mouth, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be subtle, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the hip of the hainche, and because of this the patient's limb is moved from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the patient has a departure in the region of the hips, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip of the hainche with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the limb around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three great cauterizations on the olive, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the veins; and cure until it is sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip of the hainche, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division, but the cure does not hold, and the disease is ancient: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many manners, one of which is: that you make three triangular cauterizations on the hip of the hainche in this form, and make a good depth and size, and have between each cautery the thickness of a thumb, and let the cauterizations be olive-like; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the cautery of the circle that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains all the hip and all the tendons of the knee are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And that is the way one does in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or leg. And if it reaches as far as the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations there where the patient says the pain holds, and one at the ankle four fingers to the left; and let the cauters be cutaneous, and let the tendons of the knee be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as three or four fingers below the foot or near enough, then cauterize where he feels the pain three or four times at the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary is, make him have more; and if it seems that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the cutaneous or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cauterization until you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have had a cauterization on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet as well, and it was pierced and corrupted all the feet. After a purging of the belly from which he got his death.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cauterization in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et soit eschaufez tant qu'il soit toz rouges et giete senteles,
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this fire cautery because of the fear of its regard, and if we see few who use it; and nonetheless, it is one of the good cauteries that can suffer it, and the place where it afflicts.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or striking or from too great evacuation or from similar things spread cold matter, none of these similarities is worth cauterizing except that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be freed from fetid pills or other similar things, and one should place them on their back, where the pain stays, three lines marked with a cross, and in each line .v. cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and the cauterization should be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make iij. cauterizations or iiij. at the clavicle median according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow back when they wake up, and fear; and you will find in the last part of the spine of the back and in no other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it curing, then cauterize it at the cautery of celery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	And the cautery should prick each part of the spine equally. And if you see, then cauterize around the spine at the poignant cautery .ij. lines or .iij., and let the points be close to one another. After curing, leave it so long as it is sound according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply a cautery in a spot which is in spasm of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain in the joints.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is from moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the barber calls "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterizations in this manner: make many cauteries around the jointure of the foot, and be the cauteries olive-like according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make a cautery to the whole point that we call "point". And if pains come as far as the knee and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make a cautery on each knee .iij. cauterizations or .iiij. from each part, to the whole olive-like cautery; and if you have need of more, then make more, but do not hold your hand too long until the splinters of the heart are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are to the hands, then make points around the wrist .ij. lines; and if there remains any pain to the arms, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the ribs or as far as the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good government to the patient and use medicines. For if you do good government and purge phlegm, it will be sound by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the scurvy of the syphilis.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When scurvy comes in sores, and the boils descend to the groin and it's new, then it is necessary that when you see it curing, that he does not move at all on that day; and that he uses things which loosen his bowels, so that the phlegm descends from his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his backbone until the boil is repaired, and bring them down to your knees, and mark an incision below the scurvy on the bone of the thumb, and at all a sign that is similar to the middle of a circle above the body; then cauterize it according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	So long as it is white and it emits sweat. Then bring the boils back to their place; and have the patient hold his hand above so that they do not return; and work well the thighs on the patient, and put a cushion and a servant under him on the thighs, and another one on the breast which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and steady until you reach the bone; and if you do not reach it at first, repeat it again another time until you reach the bone; and take care subtly that the boil does not burst when you make the cautery; nor burn him; so that through this the patient may not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauterizations of children be subtle according to their measure, and of grown people as great according to their measure; after that, cure the wound of butter for three days until the inflammation is gone; after that, treat other ointments until he is sound, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his nourishments be prolonged for a long time, so that the boil does not burst when he will need to go to the chamber.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, have him administered a well-made bandage, and wrap it for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, that he troubles himself little and beware of too great repletion in drinking and eating, and too high laughter; and when he does this instruction, then he is entirely sound. And I will say next about the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the scurvy of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When scrofulas come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make 1 cautery of the same type as the quantity, and let the third of the heart be burned; after that, cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the cautery to .iij. angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but mark the first sign in the cross and make one line for the breadth above the scurvy, and another below it, and put your hand through all the olive-like cautery. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pains in any member.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or injuring, and that pain persists for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "points" cautery, and the cauterization should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, virtue, and location in terms of twisting and pain. If he is sound after the first cauterization, that's good; if not, start another cauterization on top of it, because such cases are that one must change the member that is closest to him, therefore it is necessary that you make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	surgeonry
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The surgeons are aided at times by cautery with great help, and indeed the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not recede nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then do five cauteries on the head: one within the head about nine times, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand until the cautery comes to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgeonship is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head, and one cautery in the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and six on the spine of the back, and one great one on the scapula and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back, so you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I do of cauterizing, the more aid and profit it brings; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as much as the healthy person does, because the body is already too corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of iron. Afterward, care for the place with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines and oils and emplasters, but it is not healed, then make cauteries on the member according to its greatness and smallness; and let the cautery be a little way into the flesh of the knee. Then cure with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes a cautery at the hand, foot, and back, at the issue of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but however, no one interferes unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the issues of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of abscesses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine is worth nothing, then cauterize it with one cautery a little deep, according to the thickness of the flesh of the knee, until the pus is removed, and its color is changed; then cure with flour of vetches and lentils mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of calf and blood of almond, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of chancres by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When chancres come at the beginning, and you see them stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And yet wise men say to make a cautery also in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem good to me, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once or twice; and more correctly is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in dying or due to the superfluity that it makes or due to the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or due to the weather; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries in succession; afterwards leave it so. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery so that its form is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the knee, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in this manner, so that the course of the pus is alleviated. Afterward, care for it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another manner of disease exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a corruption of member, for it corrupts the members just like fire corrodes dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cauterization together with fire, then heat small and great cauteries very little by little according to what is needed at the site where the disease is; afterwards cauterize all around until you have eradicated all the corruption, so that nothing remains of it except what is corrupted. And then leave it for three days, and put on the burned places a poultice with oil as long as the eschars of fire are removed, and all the corruption is gone. Afterwards, cure with ointments engendering flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy skin does not form, it's good; and if not, then re-start the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted places. And this corruption has been sometimes cured with medicinal water in place of fire cauterization; but nevertheless, fire cauterization is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of medicinal water in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that on the feet outside a disease is born which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a big thing that breaks out on the foot. And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways. It's to know that one is fire cauterization, and the other is hot water cauterization. Fire cauterization is when you heat one cautery like a quill, and it is made of good iron to measure that it can penetrate the boil from all sides, and have subtle edges; afterwards put it all hot on the boil, and turn your hand all around the boil until it reaches the bottom of the boil; and then leave it so for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then make an ointment with wild marjoram leaves crushed with oil, and leave the ointment on throughout the night, and the boil will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then care for the wound with ointments engendering flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Et s'il sont convertit par defors le corps, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d'aigue chaude;
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from coldness or numbness, or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make .iiii. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the weight, and one on the stomach at the olivaire cautery; if the trembling ceases, and the health of the cold disease hastens.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes apparent on the bathed body or foul pustules come from gross corrupt matters. If it is necessary when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that the point may be seized by fire, or a long root of aristologe, or a lenticular cautery. And sometimes one cauterizes at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow any further ahead, but the superfluous matter from which they come is broken off, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at a cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tightly until the blood is stilled under your fingers, and no more flows; then apply fire to the olivaire cauteries, many small and large ones, until they are all red; then take one, whether great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery runs, and put it on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stemmed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts forth when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to apply these one after another until the blood is stemmed; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well stem it, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the three ways we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stem blood; and let it be bound and restrained in a good manner.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever attempts to stem the bleeding by binding tightly with cloths or applying hot things on top, or other similar things, if it does not help at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press tightly until it is stemmed above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often while it is very cold, so that the blood may congeal and thicken and be stemmed; and make a way forward for those things which he needs, such as cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical cures
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the causes and symptoms and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter on the head until the end, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way for those things which one wishes to find more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, dear friend, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for this reason it is necessary to exercise greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to take foolishness. For many ways of people come to cures. Some come with such a disease that they will die quickly due to the ignorance they find in their disease, and the greatness of their evil; and from these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these, some will give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful. It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about those things of which you are certain, and about which you can take and hold; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your diseases for which salvation is converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear friend, May Our Lord give you good understanding and rightness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy breath of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ended this chapter by describing it in chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have described from head to foot, so that you may find more easily those things which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of pure water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often befalls children at birth, and when the midwife holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and all those that I have seen died suddenly; and for this reason it seems to me that it is not worth bothering with such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew thicker every day until it could not be sustained; and so much moisture accumulated that it seemed dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the sphenoid, between the skull and the bone; and the operations are such that if the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then you cut a wide incision in the head; and make it as long as two nails, so that the moisture runs; and look here at the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more thickened and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the head opened up on each part, and the liquid jumps forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and this does not respond to you: then you must make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision extract the moisture entirely. After that, close the incisions with cloth and powder, and put wine and oil in them, and let it be like this until the fifth day; then dislodge, and treat the wound by tents and ointments, and let the head drain equally, and then let the patient eat dry meat without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look at or open the great extent of the abscess, and the gathering of the liquid; for sometimes it is before; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the spot where the abscess opens and the liquid accumulates, and let the liquid flow according to what you have the power; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and come forth blood, so that the patient may die from the deprivation of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of rheum.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease which is called "catarre" in the eyes or at the liver, and the disease is old-fashioned, and the treatment of medicine does not help at all, then the final cure is the fire cauterization with what will be cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then, when you see them being cut off, that the patient bend back his head; after he rubs the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient hold out his neck to one end of the cloth; then look at where the vein bites, and the veins of both sides are afterwards behind the ears, and they will respond; then mark the veins with an inkstone; then cut off one and the other with a sharp spatula, two parts as far as the bone, and it should be by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as two should pass through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will jump out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the space of three fingers, then mark with an inkstone and cut up to the bone; and what needs to be done with the blood to let it out is six cells, and by chance a little more or less, according to how the patient can tolerate, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point of syphac, then cut off the apostemes that do not come forth, then drain the wound and bind, and treat with ointments until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migraine.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes and sharp catarra, due to the moistors of tears and heats in temples and old foreskin and similar things, and medicine does not help him by ways of medical treatments and all this does not profit him at all, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient bends back his hair from his temples, and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little responded forth except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responded, then has the patient hold out his neck with some cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the liquid hot until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which is of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then raise it up with pincers, and separate well from the tissues that are below each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the needle, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers. For if it is not cut off, blood will not flow forth at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And extract the blood of six cells up to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two knots of a strong double silk thread, so that no pus may come forth before the wound has healed and there may be bleeding; then cut off the superfluous part which is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize with the cutaneous cautery up to the bone as far as the hairs are cut; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterization is aid to finish the moisture: therefore it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts on well-made tents; and when one unties them, one must be careful with dry medicines that bring forth flesh, and with tents, until he is healed; and if there is no gap in the artery as long as you are working, then hasten to cauterize by fire, or apply the place with vitriol and strain it with your hand until the blood is stopped; and if you do not have that present, then put your finger on the place so that the blood may congeal, and raise the place with cold water so that the bleeding ceases, and be strained as needed; and what is more main and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire-cutting knife, but the cutting parts should be well spaced to withstand their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the cutting parts are too close together, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have one big gap between the two cutlery, and then when you have marked with ink the two places, and you apply the hot iron on top so that it reaches up to the bone, and cut off the vein in two places; and let them be distant from each other between the two cells, for it is not sealed by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead of the chief part of the face, and it does not profit at all from the medicine one makes there, and you see the patient's face redness, and feel the forehead sensation as if from trembling; and thus oil are tense and moist so that the hairs of the papier are fallen, and the papier are heated and scalded by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to perform this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	Et l'apelerent li ancien "cure contuse", et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poils qu'il ait ou front, puis li fais .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l'une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusque neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l'incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au travers joins;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and many cloths to absorb the blood, then fill the spatula with two parts of which is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is below the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the fat that is between the two cuts right down to the suture that is on the bone, then do the same from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first cut the instrument called "culterelle", and it is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is soft, not at all sharp, and that's its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the soft edge of the instrument towards the fatty part of the flesh, and the sharp edge towards the bone, and push it in as far as it will go to the middle cut. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head down to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to what appears from the fat; and then do the same on the middle cut up to the other cut; and then extract the blood evenly, and express the wound for the taken blood; then put a cloth of old cotton in each cut, and put wet cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar on top, and watch so that no abscess forms; and on the third day untie the bandage, and administer great quantities of watered vinegar, then apply ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other remedies for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with a great and accustomed cataract, and you see the eyes small and tight, and dimming the sight, and the pupils burned; and the hair is falling out, and there is a severe pain in the forehead, and the patient is strangled; then knows by these accidents that those matters and this cataract come from many veins, and the father of medicine who knows it, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you command the patient to bend his forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead and another one from the wide side. One point. And begin from the temple on the left to the right temple, and let the incisions be up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples that move at mealtime; and when the bone is exposed, so evacuate all the blood with a sponge, and then dry between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton and linen cloth; then bind above wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, and take care not to form an abscess; when it is dressed, you should rub the bone until flesh begins to appear, then apply remedies that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of galenicals, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds in order to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear suppurations
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of three things: or grains, or beasts, or pebbles of stone, or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as ashes, vetches, peas; or flowing things, such as water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear a pebble or other thing that does not belong to the ear and does not grow in the ear, then put the ear in the sun. If you see the pebble, distill some violet oil or sesame oil, then administer an extraction; and make the patient snore with condiments, and block the nostrils when the snoring comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear above. Many times it comes out through this cure; and if it does not come out, then administer an extraction with fine tweezers, and that's its shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out through the tweezers, that's good; if not, then administer an extraction with fine forceps of small double-jawed type; and if it doesn't come out through that, then make a chain of iron and insert the head of the chain or piercing of the ear very tightly, and stop whatever is around the chain from entering with wax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then treat it firmly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this way, take a glue from which birds take their nests, and put into some instrument that is pointed for that purpose, and wrap a little cotton around; then press the glue on the pebble or whatever it is, and treat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't come out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut open the ear before an abscess forms and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient's head bleed, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty part or dependent part; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the pebble, then remove it as much as you can, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grains that are inside and they're inflamed, then administer an extraction; and if it can't come out, then administer one sharp spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision to that grain. But don't do it when you think the grains are moist because of the moisture in the ear, until you've made many pieces; then extract them with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is smooth.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the water then that falls into the ear it is necessary for the patient to use condiments first and fill the ear with old cotton. And let it be thus on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out through this, that's good. If not, take many stones according to the length of your stick, thin and light, and burn them slightly in the fire; and put one or two of these stones into the patient's ear, and then strike another stone on top of the one in the ear; and don't stop doing this with stone upon stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out entirely. And if you see, take one reed, and insert one end into the ear, and set fire to the other end so that the most of the reed is burned; then do the same thing again with another reeds as long as the water comes out, just as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small in body, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then administer an extraction with fine tweezers; and that's the easier thing to remove what's in the ear.
