En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun: if there appear any worms, then treat them with subtle tweezers; and if none appear, take a string whose form this is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it is narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle tip into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then pull firmly on the string; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey in coming out, stop around the string with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not jump forth as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find it in the treatment of distillations; and also distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, whose form this is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is of silver or tin, narrow below to a small hole, and wide above to distill; and for pressing within the distillation with one instrument of well-made bronze for this purpose, and if you see, take one scraper and wrap around the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice into it, and all that you have of medicines on the string, and the string be in the ear; then push inside the scraper to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled out of the ear; and if the patient feels inside, and the distillation is a pot heated over fire so it distills into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a small hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to men through stopping of wounds or new growth inside the ear, and these stoppings often come very far into the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes there is one pot overflowing with the hole, and one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then the one that comes very far in, if one cannot see it, is from grievous cleansing in multiple dispositions, and in that which one can see, it is necessary that you put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opacity apparent, then work with all this spatula whose form this is.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be gentle and careful in front of and behind all the way, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the opacity is from new growth or flesh of the ear, then hold it with subtle tweezers and cut lightly, until all that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opacity is very far in the ear, then take a subtle and light scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the flesh of the ear. If you sense the opacity from which the patient senses grief at hearing, cut lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and dampen in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on vitriol broth; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and replace another moistened tent made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes from the decoration, then plunge a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paperwax.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This wax that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to spread with forceps and tweezers, and cut with a spatula of its roots; then put on the glass vitriol broth.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if the wax peels off, then cauterize with a lenticular subtile cautery, and after the incision move slowly; and many times repair, until nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hellebore.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come in the eyes' wax-like things that seem like hellebore in form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the works are such: take care if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it's a light thing to know; then do the opening on the large side, then peel off each part lightly, then take with tweezers, and cut. If you can't cut without piercing a little of the paper, don't harm the patient; and if the opening is great, assemble a seam, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, don't do anything forceful, because the ointments restore it soon and bring forth flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over and take the grandine with tweezers, cut and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not harm anything; and when the grandine is cut, let a solution of salt water flow, and cure the wound of those who bring forth flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is brought forth in sheets of paper above, and this happens more often to children than to adults, and it causes great harm to their eyes; and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie on their faces again, and sleep above, and their papers below are moistened by the inflammation and appearance that has covered the exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the wound with your fingers and feel the exinach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the treatment is that the patient places their head in your lap; and then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then put it on them; and press with your fingers from one side to the other, so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make a mixture of rose water and spatula, cutting a slit of the large size, but not greater than the wound or making a wound of vinegar; and make the skin smooth in depth until you reach the exinach; and in multiple dispositions, exinach comes from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Here is the translation:
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the surgeon does not open in the beginning of the cut, so slightly enlarge the cut until he sees; then pull it as we have said, then damp cloths in air and water, and put on the bandage, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who break and put on poultices to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then heal him until he is sound. And if the apostemated part becomes hot, then apply soothing emplasters until he is sound.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs from paper grow differently than those of nature, and are whitened, they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of diseases as usual tears and softening of the papers and blurring, to the point of destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to four manners: either by fire cautery together, or by aqueous medicine as described in the chapter on cautery, and is made either by incision and suturing or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head on your shoulder, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, that's good; if not, put an awl through each thread above; and let this be at the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow below these hairs, and draw one thread above all the paper, and turn it to a razor; then make in the part beneath the paper, beneath the hairs that are grown together, from the great tear to the small one; then pull out one thread, and put beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper a figure of an oak leaf, as the sprig of myrtle, and although it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the paper being divided into.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if someone has a need to cut away a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened; then make an incision on all the surface above the two lines you have signed, and begin from the great tear to the small one; and let it be one of the cuts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle into one of the two angles of the corner, then scrape away all; then assemble the two lips with a suturing needle using one thread of fine wool, and stop the bleeding, and make the excess threads above the two circles on everything sticking together if you see fit to do so; and if not, don't bother, then leave the suturing and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without suturing anything constricting, because the paper revives with the closing of the wound and its assembly, but the suturing is deadly (as the ancients said), and it is a work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is as the sprig of myrtle, as we have recounted, with three separate needles according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what rises above the small forces equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps and the things are not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and put it in the figure; and put another thread near the great tear, and the second thread near the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above where you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suturing, and heal it until it is sound; and if an apostemate comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointments soothing.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and at times it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about incision; but the suturing in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of cauterization is according to this form: and it is that you transform the paper and make a hole within according to what I have said, and then make two cauterizations by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the surface are; and cut off at both ends of both parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above what rises from the paper from the oil, and strain the two cauterizations from both parties together; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die, dry up, and fall away, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut off the excess forces, and heal it until it is sound; and when the wound is closed, and the paper has been lifted away, and the hairs can no longer grow; and this is the form of the two cauterizations that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put one thread of soft and subtle silk on it; then assemble the threads and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm; then arrange in the chase another thread of fine silk briefly, and knot the end of the thread; then place the patient's head on your shoulder; and let it be under the sun so that the work is revealed, for this is a subtle and minute work; then put the needle through all the chase in the root of the hair grown together, and make it pierce the paper quickly as you guide it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it comes to the end of the chase on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull out the chase from below all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes forth from above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh is restored on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of the natural eyebrows, and raise it with that which you leave it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pouring of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the pouring comes into the oil, there are two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it happens by sudden wound, or cutting, or cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Et the manner of the work in this is that you cut open the wound, and release the lips from it, and put inside linens, and bind it until it heals; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first one; but work with things that soften, such as fenugreek; and rose petals or althea and flax seed be cooked, and ointments of water lily melted in some oil, and it is wrapped in a linen cloth, and this is its treatment.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in the same form as it was before; and these works that we have said are nothing but remedies for this disease, so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is beneath, which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things; and the way of working with it is that you take a needle, in which there is one double thread, and push it into the flesh, and make it pierce all the way from left to right, so that the threads come out in two pieces of flesh; then stretch the flesh over the entire needle, and cut at one broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper comes back in accordance with what is necessary, it's good; if not, then take one rasp and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cutouts on either side within the paper; and let the pieces from the two incisions be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, so that when they are assembled, the shape will be like the shape of a letter which has no "one Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity of its sides is grown below, from what follows the paper; then join the two disjoined parts and sew them together with a thread of linen; then apply the treatment for this that we have said about softening medicines and linens, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or an opening or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a linen cloth, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an engine to do everything they can to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling has occurred in the same way as the paper above is bound with white of oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary that you insert the point of a rasp under the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers until you cut what is suitable for a subtle spatula, which is not too tight nor too loose, so that the patient cannot bear having the spatula too tight or causing harm to the oil; and make your incision, from which you remove this assembled part, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and let all this assembled part be healed, and sometimes in the oil add a little salty water, and lift up sweet water and vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and place wet wool on top of it in abundance of eggs; and after three days use the colic remedy and similar things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the grime of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the grime is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles a hard scab, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moisture frozen, which when touched with iron and cooked between pincers, one cannot bear; and both forms begin near the large vein, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then coils the grime between pincers with small double loops, and stretches it above; then take a needle, and insert one hair from a horse, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little bit and push it into the grime, and make it pierce all the way to the end of the needle, and tie the grime with a thread and stretch it above, and scrape off the rest on the side of the grime that follows the prune and silk until the hair reaches the head; then cut the remaining part in the root of the vein to all the subtle spatula and small forces, and leave the natural flesh or vein as it was before incision, so that through the incision the body does not produce tears habitually; and sometimes stretch the grime only to the onyx and thread, as we have said; then scrape off everything at the soft spatula of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision, throw a little bit of broom seed into the oil and a colic remedy made from litargyris, and leave it until the next day; then apply the treatment as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the grime is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the onyx cannot enter, many times this appearance of grime is treated with medicines; and it is born as I have told in the division, and when you see it growing, work the oil of the patient, and take a spatula slightly rough according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the grime above gently, and if you see that it is not diminishing and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth into the oil a colic remedy made from litargyris and red colic and broom seed, and stop the oil until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the oil, like an aposteme grows warm, then milk it, and first cure the warm aposteme until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh at the vein causes great harm in the oil, then suspend it to the onyx, and cut off a part and not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill into the oil a red colic remedy made from litargyris.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Some men's eyelids grow red flesh at times, and cover the eyelid and restrain above the papers and turn it away from the face, and seem like a pomegranate rose; and the work is that the patient puts his head in one's hands, then opens the eyes, and cools all that flesh with suitable cloths to its condition, and sustains it by force; then cuts off the first layer of flesh, and goes on cutting until the end, and takes care not to bleed the eye during the operation; and the incision should be as we have said in the incision of the tongue and for small forces where one removes a scab, as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then anoint the eye with oil or distill red pepper juice or similar corrosive medicines, and put a cotton cloth on top of the eye with egg white, so that it may be assured of warm aposteme; and if there is nothing left, and the blood does not clot, and you doubt warm aposteme, then leave the eye and treat the warm aposteme with soothing things for aposteme; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make all flesh removed from the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you hasten the cure of each weak eye by natural means; and by accidental means, in iron work; and do not put your hand on any of these operations until you see that this member is suffering from this operation.
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Sebels are red veins that are covered on the eye, and tolerate the sight's work and weaken the eye all the time. It is necessary then to the first that you look at whether the oil is where the sebel is, if it is excessive, and there is no other disease except for the sebel; then coil it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your hands, then suspend those veins on all sides according to your wisdom, and be the ligatures subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two ligatures by degree in one piece according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the forces those veins subtly, and remove the blood hour after hour, until you see removing those veins from the eye; and take care not to bleed the eye at all points of the scalp, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut off more than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red pepper juice into the eye to corrupt what remains of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all of that in one hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyelids, and let it be some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured of warm aposteme, then resume according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the abscess of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon so calls "arissati" abscess: when you cure it by cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a reason in it that you cut into the aposteme, where it should decay, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then replace it with all the instruments that are there according to this form; and it is called "aspre chief", and make it from iron into one chief bent, and be pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this some times, then restore the surface with excitative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the bone is hardened, and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is hardened, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not heal and is not apostemated, and bad accidents come, then know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other reason than to bring the fistula back to its original place according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with burning medicines, and when it is uncovered take one force according to this form, and be the key of iron at three angles, and the bolt should be tempered until the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the bone near the socket, and remove your hand from the eye a little, then turn the whole force until it pierces the bone and the patient feels by this that the blood flows if they hold their hand on their neck; and then restore the surface with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the bone, the matter will go to the neck; and it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyelids open fully and it does not come out of the neck or decrease, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal him, then put poultices or bandages made from iron to suck up, then put a lien on the eye made from aloes, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and drapes; and the manner of the drapes is that you take soft drapes, and double each one in four, and then put one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye has need of; then strain it above a strong binding cloth, and repeat the poultices to suck up without causing harm; then remove the poultices and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the lien becomes worn out, then it is necessary that you restrain it much; then remove the lien after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good; if not, then repeat the plastering and draping and liening and poultices until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the bursting of the vitreous humor
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the vitreous humor, then it bursts forth, and comes out like a grain of resin, and it is so astonishing to see; then if you see it burst, the operation is such that you insert an awl into the root of the part below just up to the top, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the socket; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the vitreous humor around, and strain it well, then remove the awl and put on the eye a damp linen cloth soaked in egg white; and let it be until the threads choose with the vitreous humor, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vitreous humor in each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes show great appearance, then puncture with a subtle spatula that comes from beneath the eyebrow, and correct the moisture albugina and descend the eyelids, and enter it in short order; then pull it out until it is clean.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bottom of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not other than the lower part that is assembled in the eye, resembling a drop descending, and it's not a drop; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on one prepared seat and straight, then take their head between your two hands and gently move it until you see the lower part come up to your eyes; then it will be inserted, and not descend and become disheveled the light, and the patient will see things as they used to; and if it does not go down below, know that it's a drop, and if the descent of the lower part is not prepared as we have said. Then make the patient sit in your hands, then take the subtle spatula and insert it above the corneal tissue one point at a time by the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal tissue and the crown, until the lower part comes out; and when it is issued, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey or water or fenugreek boiled with honey, then be treated with another cure until it is clean.
des aigues de l’oil	from the tears of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the similarities of tears in division and what is necessary to pierce; then work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit in your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and tie the healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then place the point of the instrument beneath the cornea by the thickness of a nail in that corner of the eye near the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" gently and turn your hand until it pierces into the corner of the eye, and sense that almagda comes to the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the forefront of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the night; and that is the cornea of the eye; then you will see bone on that paper by the brightness of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument just above or where the tear is, and press it down one way after another. If the tear now descends, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, and if the tear rises again by the second path, place the force with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently pull out almagda by rotating your hand little by little; then put in a small amount of this gemstone, and leave it inside the eye. Then place a poultice or a wet cloth on the eyelid made from rose oil and abundant egg white, and bind with the healthy eye. Now, and those who are of our time, we apply a common broth with abundant egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", whose shape is:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then puncture the conjunctive only, and do not go too far into it, but make a subtle point, and then insert almagda as we have said; and upon the completion of the work, prepare for the patient one a gentle bed, where he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and let him rest according to his disposition until the third day; then release him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the tie up until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but rather hasten this, because the tear rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If the abscess is inflamed, you should release the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the abscess; and when it is pacified, then release the sight and put on his face a little wickerwork to cover for some days, and let him stay in that dark house. And then come out of the house slowly and gradually, and convert back into his own condition; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the land of Yrach, who told us that in his country he had seen someone make almagda pierce, which causes tears to flow, but I never saw anyone do this in our land, nor did I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see; and they are properly from iron.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of these is made of this same subtlety, and the end in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin on the nail
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At no time do nails or nail skins come together in diverse forms, of which there are some that resemble scorpions by many feet; and if there is such a one with skin enchanced by fiery color, or skin soft of bone color. In that then of these skins which is soft, and not at all enchanced, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the juice on those skins, and treat them gently; then take what you can sustain with a subtle spatula from one side, until you know that this skin is entirely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be removed, then open it with all the subtle instruments gently, until nothing remains; and if without stirring or aposteme inflamed, then proceed as is necessary; and if it is malignant apostemes, then hasten and cauterize as much as possible, until the wound is stanchied and all the skins are removed; then pour in wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nail works and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is skin born in the bone above, which prevents the instruments from coming: then it is necessary that you put a piece of linen thread about the size of a finger, well oiled by hand, with about one or two inches between each knot; and make the patient place the end of the thread in his nose to his power, and guide it through the nostrils until it comes out at the mouth; and this is done many times for children at school, and it is a light thing for someone who wants to do it. Then hold one end of the thread that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and let them go in succession as we are on the thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that skin, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose just as before; do this for three days or more, until all remaining skin is corroded by the ointments; and then place a piece of linen cloth on the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs medicinal poultices, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, which distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Et soit d'argent ou d'arain, semblant à une lampe ouverte, si comme une cainne, et li conduis ausi;
de la char sor le neis	On the skin above
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a sickness called "telul" arises on the skin above the navel; it grows and becomes great in size until it is a visible thing to behold; and therefore it is necessary that you cut off the top, and remove all fat, then place the cautery or burning medicine upon it; and if one delays in cutting until it is great, take heed lest it become hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts into it at any time, a great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul color, and you see that you can cut it all off, then empty the patient and cut off the abscess without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continued healing comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, more than in some people. It is therefore necessary to act thus with each, if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then place the two lips together, sew them up as much as they will stretch, and cure until they are healed; and if the lips have already become separated on one side or the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their keratinizing so long as they bleed, then put the two lips together again, bind, and powder with blood of dragon, and incense bruised; and place upon the powders a piece of ointment of good or another ointment suitable, and let it be until it cures by itself, then cure with oil until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses within the lips that are hard, resembling grains of millet, and smaller or larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each notch, and take out the contents with pincers and cauterize each part; then apply a poultice to the area after incision of vitriol bruised, until the blood is staunched; and then leave the lip open, and cure the area with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the skin of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth called "albulus" arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut off at its root, and let the bow or blood flow; then place upon the area vitriol bruised, or other drying and desiccating powders; and if that growth returns after incision, and many times occurs, then cut it off again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; therefore it is necessary that you sit the patient in your hands, and his head be in your sight, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness and jaundice and other discolorations, until they are cleansed; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it is good; but if not, then continue to repeat the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need diverse forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, for this reason that the rasor used to scrape away the teeth has other forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay drawing out as long as you can, for it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance just up to where one has no excuse for drawing.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to draw out, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth's fault. Many times the pain makes the patient think she has a holy tooth and has a good tooth drawn out; and yet the pain does not depart from her through this, until the bad stuff comes out, for we have already made to go away these saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth's fault, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth in all its splendor, as much as possible, strong enough to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it to your hands or subtle forceps at the first pace and pace, until it is well extracted, then secure the forceps; and have the patient's head in your sight between your knees, and hold it thus so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side slightly, and move it as you did initially. And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it is necessary that you fill it with drapels, where the perforations are; and then extract it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break while being strained; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take good heed that you do not break it, and leave a part, and the root returns to the patient with even greater pains than the first. And take heed that you do not act like foolish sages who, through their haste and boldness, sometimes break the chariot and do not bring what we have recounted; but rather bring great sicknesses by the roots that remain or by the chariot that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with vinegar or oil and salt; and if blood comes out of the wound, which often happens, apply the area with vitriol bruised; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments with which one should extract teeth first are those with long points and thick handles, so that they do not double back on you when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting, and should be made of well-forged iron, and should have teeth to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at extraction, it is necessary that you put a moistened cotton pad on the wound .i. day or two, until the wound is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefri", with which the wound seems to take on the shape of a comb; and should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is also known as "palainche", of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is strong and thick so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out by this means, that is good; but if not, then help it with all the instruments, of which the forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument that has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in proportion to the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters skilled in themselves find their instrument, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are some diseases where the ancient ones did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of bones and flesh, or it breaks on the bone or on another bone, or it can, then seek out the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and aid with gestures, of which this is the form:
