Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-held to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone, and it is small, then reduce all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural bodily form, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young maidens, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be soothed or trimmed: then file; and if it is rough with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the form, and it is similar to one small beak, and let it be made of iron with a sharp point above:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the edge is worn away little by little over a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can trim it, then use a file like this in its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little over a few days gradually, so that it does not move until it is even; then smooth out the end of all roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and hurt the tongue, then file off the roughness as much as needed, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on what they eat lest they fall out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and it does not work; then it is necessary to restrain them with a thread of gold, for silver threads become green and putrid, but gold ones never change; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are directed, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the knots between the bad teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and slowly, so that it does not move; and let your finger be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then file the knots of the thread with pincers, and assemble them, and re-point between the healthy teeth, and place it thus so that it does not hurt the tongue; then leave it this way as tight as it can remain, and if it breaks or the threads rot, then restrain it with another thread; if it remains and serves in this way throughout its lifetime, and that is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, gradually and step by step, as we have said; and do not meddle with it if you are not wise and skilful, and at times make the shape of a whalebone tooth, and put it in the place where the defect is, and restrain it as we have said, and remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue by nature, or by accident of an old wound; and the work is such that you must open the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your hand, and lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament of the wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its seat, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it is a recent wound, then apply an unguent and cut off the ligament; and be sure the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, then lift up the rose-colored cloth and let it dry, or use cold water, and then place a linen tent under the tongue; and leave it on each night, so that the wound cannot heal. And if bloody discharge comes forth, then put vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood flows, then cauterize with the slow fire, which is good for this; then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see that it is of foul color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards gangrene, and there is moisture, then apply an unguent, and cut a small opening with a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the wound flows at your operation, then put vitriol powder on it until it is stopped, then return to your operation until you have done everything; then lift up the linen cloth and dry it, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes an abscess called "godath" comes inside the throat, and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hard and small abscess of foul color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the reason of bloody discharge; but let it stay until it dies, and then you will open it or it would break apart by itself; and if it is a white abscess that reopens, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument to cut, but examine first whether the abscess is at rest and appeased. Then have the patient sit before the sun, with their hands in your hand, and open their mouth and take hold of the servant between their hands, and press the tongue below the entire instrument, which is the form; and it should be made of silver or subtle lead, like scissors:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue all over this instrument and see the abscess, then take a needle and thread it through the amber, and pull it tight above as much as you can; and leave nothing loose with the threads, then shape the instrument accordingly, so that it has the form that appears to be some force; and although the head is curved, and one end to another, and are very sharp, and made of iron or flint.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then shape it with pliers, so that it has the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make it taper from one end to the other; and when you have shaped one of the amber pieces, then shape the other in the same way; and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and if blood vessels appear, gargle the patient again; or use cooked apple pulp, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then continue to cure until they are healed; and sometimes new abscesses arise in the throat that are like the two amber pieces, so shape them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely one of little sense; and I had already closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked conduit, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she had remained like this for a day or two. The abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two rains through the two openings of the nose. I hastened then, and threaded a needle, then pulled it tight, and removed a great portion of blood; then I refixed the other part in the other opening of the nose, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I threaded the needle into this abscess, and cut off a part, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus was unblocked the conduit of the woman's throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back, and filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I bound it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the vein descends to the vein, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a thick and rounded one, it is called "vein". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to cut it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and it is sanguine or of a rusty color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision on it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we mentioned earlier; then thread a needle into the vein, and pull it tight, and cut off one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two ambers. And it is necessary not to cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; because if you cut more, you will harm the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two ambers, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of cutting, then it is necessary to use a trick for the cauterization without fear. The manner of the cautery is hot water. And it is that the patient puts their head on your shoulder, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and confesses with warm water, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in using this instrument, so that it has the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient's head on a pillow or a cloth, just as hair is placed in a comb, and put the instrument on all of the medicine on the vein; and the patient should sit up straight on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, without going down to the throat and wound. Then hold your hand on all of the medicine and press it on the vein for the length of half an hour, until you see it turn white and the medicine's inflammation is appeased; and if you see anything, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in the cane above, until the cotton reaches the vein; and do this many times until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start the medicine's cautery again, start it again, and afterwards apply a poultice around the vein with butter, and purify everything that surrounds the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and cured by gargling until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them into one pot, and add a little water, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with clay from a hard earth, and inside the pot have one instrument carved according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and one of the keys should be inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the vein through the tube, until the vein is suffocated; afterwards, repeat this often, until the vein dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the abscess' heat, for many things happen then; and don't do it more than at the decline of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a tube and put an eggshell into the patient's mouth so that their mouth doesn't get too hot; for the eggshell doesn't allow the vapor to bother the mouth, and it is a good cure together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it seems to be stuck in the throat like a bone or a fish spine, or something else; so it is necessary that you try what you can see and press the tongue on the sun with all the instrument, until you see the thing move; and whatever does not appear and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the top, it will be stuck, and then you will pull it out further; and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the top so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted high up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, lest all life depart from him, nor push the bone inside; and make sure the patient puts the instrument in place, because the thing is awkward; then push down, or pull it out fully with all the instrument equally, until it is fully out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the phlegm of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No time is medicine for the phlegm, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at noon, because you press the tongue to the instrument that I told you. And if you see the phlegm, then pull it out with a small hook or fine forceps worth doing. And if that doesn't work, take a braided string and put it in the throat of the patient, then push the hot iron into the string's knot, and do this often. And if the patient is bothered by water all day, then take a full view of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it down without swallowing, and move it to their hand often; and as soon as the phlegm feels the water, it will settle.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it doesn't settle as we said, then suffumigate the patient with asefetide at the instrument that I told you in the fumigation of the ear; do this many times, for it will settle without much trouble. And the manner of the fumigation is to take a pot that has hot coals in it, and have the pot covered with a pierced cloth in the middle, and in that perforation be the key of the instrument; then pour your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the head of the pipe in their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes just to the phlegm; and the phlegm will settle now, and if it doesn't settle, then resume the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and drink no water; and then it is necessary that it goes forth through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the phlegm is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps for entering the throat; and it has a resemblance to a surgeon's beak, and on it there is an asperity of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and look at this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many types of abscesses are, according to what is remembered hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners in which one is similar to the other, and that which holds moisture. And the second manner is for those who are at the bone or in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the bruised place are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if the abscess is not to be pierced until the swelling subsides according to its completion; and there are those which need to be pierced when they are hard, and do not subside according to their completion, such as the abscesses that come in joints. For when abscesses come in joints, and one leaves them until they are all around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, thereby causing contraction in that member. Or the abscess is at the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it subsides, it will harm the principal member; or if it is at the foundation, then one should pierce it as soon as it subsides; and it is not necessary to pierce a hard abscess without digestion being complete, except for that which is at the foundation, lest it burrows inwards and becomes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess which is soft according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and of the swelling and firming up of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where the abscess appears more dependent on its location, and where it opens outwards; and the perforation should be made from long to short in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints, nerves, or arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that are painful, according to the member. And when abscesses are in bruised places, it is better that you leave the perforation until they are confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them before then, the body of the venom will be prolonged, and it will be filled with a great deal of ordure; and by chance the lips and the profundities of him may harden. And for any abscess that needs to be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member requires. And it is necessary that you make small perforations for small abscesses, and large perforations for large abscesses, and many openings according to the appearance of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut off the key, and cover; when it has become as worn out as a piece of cloth, and is no longer nourished, then one should do as one does for babies: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those whose covering is done like the foliage of myrtle, such as abscesses of the kidneys; and if there are those where one makes a round shape, and other shapes and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those that have no head, such as a soft abscess on the surface, it is necessary that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has accumulated great swelling, and you pierce it, not to remove all the swelling at once, but to remove part of it; then stop the abscess up until the next day, and do not touch anything above; do this by degrees, as long as the swelling goes away; likewise if the patient is weak in virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. For the expectations sometimes tremble with the issue of the swelling, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not be aware. Therefore, proceed with great caution through this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, sew up the wound; and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a plain cut, insert tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put one tent in each so that they come together against each other; and if you have removed part of the skin from the abscess and wrapped it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or flax cloth without moisture, and tie it up until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se decorremens de sanc avient à ton ovraige, si aménistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor leu décorant par maintes fois.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have told you how one should proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and see chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Wherever a boil comes on the head, they are small abscesses, and they are like the cocoons of silkworms, just as a spider spins its web; and many resemble this. There are some that are fatty and similar to poultices; and there are those that are dry and stony hard to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make it difficult. And the works of cutting are such that you test all .i. instrument called "entromissoire", from which its form comes next, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, one makes it above the long one. And when the moisture is emptied, one scrapes without leaving any skin containing that moisture, for it returns immediately if one leaves anything; then dip in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound, and leave until the next day; and those who are left of the night. And then re-dip the cotton, just as before, on the second day, and again on the third day, until you know well that it does not stay at night; then cure the wound with ointment as necessary, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds one night's fatness, cut it according to this form, from the long one; and pour out your poultices, and scrape off all around, and put all your care of drawing forth from the skin where it lies; and if the artery makes it difficult for you, do what I told you afterwards. And similarly with the abscess if it is stony, and of cutting and curing just as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the stony abscess and the moist one is easier, because they are full of blood. And if there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and one of these abscesses that I cut open on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a dry stone, hard and white, and could not break it; and if one had done anything to it, one would have made as much of a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent place, so that the bow may issue forth; and cure them as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck and below the armpits, and in the angles, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are joined together. And each scrofula is properly within its own coat, just as the boil and the abscess of the head, as we said; and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are malicious ones that do not wish to obey health. Therefore, when you see a good disposition in the touching, and it is similar in color to the body, and quiet from each side, and is not hard on the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut it above, and scrape off each part, and let the two lips of the boil open, if you need it, just as we said in abscesses of the head; and draw forth bit by bit, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor should the spatula be agitated or tearing, lest your hands escape, and you see too far ahead, lest you do not cut what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not leave you to work, then put in the wound a vitriol or broom, or some powders that stop blood, and close the wound; and let it stay until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it; then look at the sign of what remains if there are any small scrofulas, cut them off and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, it does not need that you cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you gather up the two lips of the wound, and sew them together now, so that there is no remaining superfluity due to the greatness of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand how to cut at its root, and draw forth, and sew as we have said. Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce there where it appears; and pierce it in this way, depending, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment releasing flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of squinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and talked about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinsy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat, which is called "epiglote", be opened; and one does not make aid by this, because all the veins and the prominence of the patient are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the prominence of the neck, it is necessary to cut open the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we want to cut open the epiglote, that we cut it under three circles or four a small slit from side to side, between the two circles or according to the size of the abscess's opening, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and this is suitable for the section of the epiglote that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the entire wound, then cuts open the boil until it comes to the channel; and stop the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut out the abscess, just as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the blood from the channel which jumps forth through the broken ligament and by the failure of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed about which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with care, and sew all together without leaving any cartilage; then administer medications that cause flesh to grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Also it says that one should not do this just yet until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and his life is slipping away.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut off the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and therefore the ancient ones command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maid take one knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the veins of the groin;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure him, and I found him just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and saw well that it had not yet been drained or led away from the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was sound.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the maid except that she regained her voice, and then returned to her normal condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting off the epiglottis one should have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the greenish color of jasper, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or the natural one has no deceit.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which resembles fat tumors, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it is not to be feared, and one should not hesitate to operate on that which is small, and test and search all the surrounding tissues.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like a small fatty tumor, and it cannot be drained by any vein, then cut it off, as one cuts off tumors, and treat it all around, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well all around, and heal it as it should be, until it is perfectly sound.
des nous	of the tumor
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of tumors, and I will tell all their likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is fitting that I tell the whole difference which is between tumor and abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, until the suppuration has passed away, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the tumor there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains a pus-filled sac, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the body, and begins just like a greenish-yellow abscess, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two likenesses, either fatty or moist, and much of the color is as I have said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the tumor, that you examine and investigate first all the instruments that are called "surrounding" tissues, according to what its form will be or chapter which comes later.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses of tumors is that you take or more moistened tool than what you find in the abscess, and turn your two probes back and forth, until you know that the instruments have pierced the skin, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the surrounding tissue, and take note in what it bursts forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moist discharge is greenish or yellowish, then proceed as I have said about other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the surrounding tissue no moist discharge comes, knows it is fatty, then proceed to cut it in crosswise fashion, and take hold of it with pincers, and scrape it lightly from each part, and preserve the edge or corner where you find it healthy along with the tumor.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot remove it intact, then remove it in pieces, so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return the tumor many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if only a small piece remains and the blood grieves you, then apply a caustic powder to the wound, and stop the bleeding, and place soothing things on the hot abscess, and heal it with other remedies until it is sound.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the tumor is large, then sew up the two lips of the wound, and heal it with those things that promote flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another obstacle is contrary to your action, and you hasten and apply a poultice of vitriol, and let it lie two or three days or until the wound purrs, and the pus settles; then return to cutting off what remains of the tumor.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of surrounding instruments, and they are of three kinds: great, middle-sized, and small; and there are also three squares that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, middle-sized, and small, to investigate abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews sorceries, and they are of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most valued, and are more tried in black lead to investigate the cavities of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three kinds: great, middle-sized, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the orifices.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the lancets are many likenesses, as you see here: great, middle-sized, and small; and there are also lancets that have two orifices of three kinds alike.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are lancets that have three orifices, and they are also of three kinds; and there are lancets that have two orifices, and single lancets with one orifice, and they are all of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these lancets are cutting, and there are some that do not cut very far from one side, with which we remove the tumors, so that one does not cut into the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introgressors are the alemeles replied in girdles, so that the patient is not aware of the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and there are three kinds: great, small, and middle, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use more than in a well-proportioned body, such as legs, arms, and hips, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the scions of fistulas, according to this form, in which blood is staunched;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes at the place that heals completely from veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should follow this form of the line b until g;
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicated grease, then bring together the two lips of the wound at the seam, and cure it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs down and is loosened by its size like it is in women, then cut it into two folds above, with two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b until line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about seams and powders, and everything necessary for the cure, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest or due to the decomposition of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the remaining fat and grease have melted away, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard forms of scrofula or if it has nodules, and some of them contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Then those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b until line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment according to this form until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, then cut it as we have said in incisions for scrofula, and if the wound yields pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn shut, then many abscesses come, and it also happens that the vein swells and becomes an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscess is long and deep inside.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it in your arm, you will feel one strangeness; and when it is due to the vein, then it will be swollen and appears forth.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and neck and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is then necessary to avoid ironing the wound, and also for him who is at the head, and in that which is swollen from artery, cut above the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the size of the abscess, and separate the artery from the flesh, so that it is fully exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle below the abscess, and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then tie the place between the two ties with an introgressor so that the blood that is there will issue out, and relieve the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the ointment that draws pus, until the tie breaks.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with ointment according to this form, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the swelling of the vein, then it is necessary that you anoint with your hand all that you can of the abscess and the entire skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle below the place that you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce through, and have one double thread, so that you can draw it out from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or tie one end of the two parts of the thread to the other two chisels of the file.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not long enough, then insert another needle along all of the thread below the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess pus issues out, then cut off the excess fat and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then apply remedies of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses in the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come to the artery and vein when they are ruptured or due to excessive strain, so too do abscesses come to the kidneys when they are fatigued or from excessive labor and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens in the armpits and arms, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is accompanied by many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one strains strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depths of the body, but rather below the fat.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it hurts all over, and does not move forward or backward, nor up or down, and the one who is in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one who is on the head or forehead, make the skin at the eyebrow.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then take hold of it with forceps and cut it off at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is large, suspend it on the gallows, and flay it, then extract the bone and assemble the wound to the seam, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great hanging lips
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in wombs and not elsewhere in the same way, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the roots are subtle and the swelling great; and there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen in a man who had two in his womb which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had small roots, and were torn apart, and immediately began to exude moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6, and the work in the incision is that you see if the patient is moist, and the color of the articular fluid is white and moist and of fine roots.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if you cut the spatula wide and are present at the burning cauterization; For when cutting comes often too great a bleeding of blood, and if the blood overflows, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient is frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one well-made linen thread and bind the articular fluid as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to strain the linen thread until you have cut the articular fluid, and take care by this means; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut further because of the womb, but you can well cut half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not recur; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the articular fluid which is of foul color and poor sense and with regard to milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess infected by enchantment, and I will come to the cure of abscess hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cauterization of a wound or an incision for syphilis, and it is on the belly and in some of the boils, as it happens with other swellings, or from blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is due to the swelling of syphilis and by the exit of pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears with diverse exit.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press it with your fingers it springs back, and then returns, and by chance it may be solidified, and greatly swells at the entrance of the bath and through great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and appears well when you press it with your hand, not constraining at all; and if it is due to blood, then it appears by these signs as a big and hard abscess, and is fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, then it hurts at the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment. For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the boil, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the boil.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to lie quietly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place where you have signed all over the spatula,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then cut off half of the abscess above all the great incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or a tight silk cord, and have the knot be firmly secured.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the half of the abscess stretched out above the ligament, and put your finger's index into it, and cut the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it bound by the ligament, then untie it, and put the intestine outside of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, then take hold of it on the gallows, and cut away the superfluity.
