et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein gives you trouble, then go around it well, and come back to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape as if you were piercing.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in three places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it can be done, and take care of the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and ready, then treat it as necessary, and shape the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as necessary, and close the wound.
dou chancre	of the abscess
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the appearances of abscesses, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid iron treatment; and we say that abscesses are born in marshes, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients say that when abscesses are in a place or can be reached as if it were in the very flesh, and in the groin, and in similar places, one should remove it all at the beginning; and when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal from it, nor has anyone healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place or can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black bile at times; then make them healthy if they have manifest repletion; then prepare the patient a good place to do the work; then throw your gallows or abscess, and shape it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow out completely, and inspect the wound with your hand or some other thing; and if the bleeding of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it so that the blood is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division about the appearances of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment that is done with medicines, and that which is cured with iron: it is shone solely; and one should not touch iron on these two appearances: namely, tympanites and hydropisic rupture, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this appearance of dropsy, which is called "eclites" of medicines, and the treatment does not benefit, look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as a twisted stomach and similar things; do not touch iron then, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient with great vigor, and he has no other illness except pure dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Have the patient sit straight up with their hands and the attendants press the belly to push the water down to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spathium spinous according to this form: And be cut off at .ij. parts to a point, yet not so much that it can come to the intestine when it is inserted, and cannot injure;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, it is necessary that you cut on top of the belly .iij. inches right above the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then make the incision on the left side of the belly .iij. inches; and if it's due to spleen, then make it on the right side, and do not let the patient lie on top of the incision so that excess fluids do not flow to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and plug it, and lift your hand to all the spathium spinous between the skin and the syphac just like in shearing to the quantity of an fingernail or around; then pierce the syphac until the spathium spinous comes to the right width, and that is the measure of water, then treat it further, and plug this instrument which is the form: And it resembles a subtle silver chain, and is made of lead or lighter archaean ore, and has in the lower part .i. small perforation; and on one side, .iij. perforations; and .ij. on the other side, and .i. on another; and the handles are cut like a feather, and that is the form of the incision which the writers fashion the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instruments come to the water, then pour now onto the instrument; empty it then one-third or two-thirds, for if you empty more than it's necessary at this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit of their arm, or they become faint, or approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty according to the quantity of their strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now because of the key that stops the perforation which is on the syphac, of which I spoke, that you pierce in this manner; then start the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw out a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this for a few days, and take care not to let out too much water. And if you doubt the patient, and leave out a lot of water, the cure will be for burial or sand heat, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and drinking; and the cure of drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	No child is born without a perforation in the penis, or the perforation is small, or it is not in its place. If this is necessary, then it must be pierced at each spathium spinous very subtly according to this form: then insert into the perforation .i. thin plug of lead, and tie it up and hold it thus for .iij. days or iiij., and when they want to make urine, then remove the plug, and let them urinate, and then put it back; and by chance there is no need, because the urine that comes forth does not allow the plug to remain closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who have small perforations are treated with lead plugs, as we said, and it will expand. Those who do not have the perforation in its place are injured, for no one is born with the perforation at the top of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis up; and cannot void because the matter cannot come to the opening, and that is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of treatment is that the patient lies on their back, then place the head of the penis and cut it as one would shape a quill, so that the perforation opens in the middle, as it should; and be careful not to let blood flow from it which often happens, and if it does, stop it with something that stops bleeding, and cure the wound until they are healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; and it is necessary that you take them at one time very subtly, and cut and clean all of them, then put a damp cotton swab in Egyptian oil; then treat with divine ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil is malignant, with foul color and smell, it is necessary that you apply a cautery. When you have cut it open, and the boil is on the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the boil that is inside first; and when it is closed, then treat the outside part. For if you cure it together, it is not certain that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come into its place and on the crown; therefore it is necessary to remove everything that is black and corrupted, then bind with an ointment made from the rind of green pomegranates and dates, and then treat with other remedies until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterization is useful for two dispositions together: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert a lead wire into the urethra of the penis, and let the patient urinate in between; and when the skin at the top of the penis which has not been circumcised becomes inflamed because of injury or abscess, then it is necessary to shave with a sharp instrument as much as possible until the bond is loosened, and the head of the penis be freed from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if this is a difficult thing to do, it is necessary that you shave with a spathium spinous some little bit from the top of the penis and skin; then shave carefully between two points, and put a thin linen cloth damp in cold water on it so that it does not become inflamed again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the cutting off of continuity like other wounds; however, when we do this work by our own will and especially for children, it is necessary that we make the best possible work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have asked the greatest part of masters and saints who performed circumcision around one day, with great forces, and all a new moon; so it was the case where there are two skins, and by chance if you cut the top one and leave the bottom one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is to cut, and there is double pain, and the point of the member is not ensured; and at the mundification of the tongue by chance escapes the iron, and hinders the work, and many times it happens thus that they do not need mundification and I have asked.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mundification that is done with force, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally well in one smooth motion; but let the thread be very taut around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing more than simply wrapping the thread around the penis, and then allow him to go in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make it stay between your hands straight, and repeat the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow or cut, and bring it up as far as the head of the penis is; then clean well from the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the loose end with a double thread, then tie below one piece to another; and hold it in place by the second tie at the pouch and at the right index, and cut between the two ties, then lift the top quickly and bring the head of the penis.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for it is the mothers; and put powder on top and on top of the powder one sheet glued with a yolk of cooked egg mixed with rose water, oil, good and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure him with another cure until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for the mundification is this: the two fingers should be held and should be pressing, and should be equal in length.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the bleeding inside flows out at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the edges make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot keep it at your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, then let it be until the abscess has subsided, and scrape lightly; then cut as much as you can move, and take care not to harm any part of the penis.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with sudden bleeding powder, which we have said or treated in the treatment of powders, and if you cut too much with the knife, and it goes above, then it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until he is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the kidney, or frozen blood, or bowel, or charcoal born, or similar things, which we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to kidney obstruction in the loin or neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bent forward on his knees; and his feet should be placed on the back, and extend his belly from above to the back, and restrain the patient's movements as much as he can; and then constraining the neck of the bladder by expressing the kidney above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", of which this is the form: and be made of silver fine, thin, and curved like a bird's feather; and be about one and a half palms long, and be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it at the top with a piece of wool or cotton, and put the tip of the thread inside the siringue; and cut off the excess of the thread and put it just to the top of the siringue, then anoint the siringue with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and dry water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then put the siringue lightly into the penis, so that it comes to the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the pubic area; then insert the siringue forward just to the bladder, and the patient feels the urine coming out just to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless the channel or passage through which it flows is twisted; then pull the thread along the entire length of the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then draw it out, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the siringue until the bladder is empty, and soothe the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or bleeding comes into the bladder, or putridity is assembled, and you see distilled waters and medicines, then make all the instrument called "clepsedre", and this is the form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the edges are curved so that the medicine can be applied in such a way that it stops well without adding anything, and then we can draw out the moisture, and apply when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see that your medicines are in the bladder, put the tip of the cauterizer into the moisture, and pull the cauterizer back to the point where it is; then draw out the moisture with the cauterizer, and then apply strong force to the cauterizer again; then the moisture will go in and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle clepsedre with which one cleisters the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or archaunt, and the key is higher up; and below it there is one seam or the strings lie; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see cleisterring the bladder into it, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat one end of that moisture over the fire; then put the tip of the clepsedre into the penis, then strain your hand over the bladder in such a way that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	et if thou hast not the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make one circle and pierce it all around roundly then put in one strong thread into these holes then assemble the circle as one assembles one tile and put inside that which you see oil water and moisture and tie up the instrument and do so as you have done with the bladder to press with thy hand until the moisture comes out of the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and together with medicines and we have said the difference between the stone that is born in the reins and all the signs and in which stone one must work by cutting and in the bladder and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is born in the bladder is more common in children and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and then hair forms, and the patient's penis becomes hardened and inflamed, and it happens many times, and then it subsides; and many of these stones fall into the foundations; and childhood cures are much lighter until they have three years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is at its mean between youth and old age; and the cure is more light for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purge the patient with a laxative in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders finding the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and lift them up and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes falls from a high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then search for it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the bladder, then hasten now to cut above the stone. And if it does not fall at all with the touch, moisten your two middle fingers of oil from your left hand if the patient is an infant, or your two middle fingers of oil from your right hand if the patient is a young adult; and insert them into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your fingers, then move it to the neck of the bladder; then press above on your fingers, and push it forward where you see the cutting place.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand above the coils, and with his left hand take away the skin that is below the coils in the part where you are making the cut; then put the spatula together, so it forms.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make a cut between what is between the coils and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left naively; and be straight above the stone, and your two fingers should be at the foundation, and the cut should be wide behind, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the pressure may cause the stone to jump far away with little effort; and know that there are some stones which have angles, and margins: it is grievous to come out; and there are those which are below, resembling a shell, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that stone which has angles and margins, make the cut more large; and if it does not jump, it is necessary to stretch above with the pincers which are like a file at the head, in order to strain the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below one of those instruments with a curved head; and if you cannot manage it thus, then widen slightly the hole, and if the blood flows, then constrict it with vinegar.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, then first remove the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it out, and the small ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, then it must be split, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: or he dies, or urine comes out immediately by the way that the flesh cannot heal; but still strive to remove it, or dismember with pincers, until you pull it apart piece by piece.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and compress it, and put over it a damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot aposteme; then resupply the patient on his back, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, then arise very well the wound of oil and water, and then anoint him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot apostemes come to the wound and corrosion, and congealment of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by that which flows like urine: then put your two fingers into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and destroy it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound with water and azole and silk, and help him in all ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, that you bind his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the bed.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra of the penis and stuck inside, and urine cannot come out; then cure him as I have said before, that you cut into him many times, except for this cure by cutting. I have already tried it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and be fixed at three angles in one handle:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the rod into the penis lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the rod in your hand in the small hole and small hole, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if urine comes soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. If it breaks off, it will jump out with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and another above, then bend the penis towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and release the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure him until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does happen, then the treatment is grievous, and it is defended against three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-known woman who will uncover herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more inward than the stone of man, therefore it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity summons you to this, then it is necessary that you take a wise woman well-versed, and find one who knows how, and if you cannot find one, not at all ask one chaste subtle mirror; and the present one, give a good old wife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command from the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to strengthen her fundament and seek out the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her fundament, and command her to strengthen her fundament with the patient, and gently press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to beneath, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, there where it is most apparent, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her bowels above or below the stone, and be the incision at first small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then bind the cord in the incision, if you feel the stone so far along the wound until the stone can issue forth; and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and great, rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with ridges; and know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood overflows, then put vitriol powder at the place, and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stayed; then return to your work, until the stone is forth, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones from men to aid you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood overflows, and it is from the artery that was cut, then put powder on the place and strain of tents and bandages, and do not continue this any longer, and let the stone be and do not pull it out at all, lest by chance the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the place is clean, then return to your work until the stone is forth.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramace aquouse is nothing else but the gathering of moisture or white leucorrhoea, which is below the skin of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "leucorrhoea", and sometimes it is properly in the web of the egg, if one thinks it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white leucorrhoea that we have said; and this does not happen unless there is nothing.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramace is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and it is spread out in that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it is declining towards yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is the white leucorrhoea that we have said, then there is the abscess of rens, a long one like the figure of an egg, and does not open the testicles, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper web, then it is the abscess of rens with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white leucorrhoea, then it feels like one knows well; therefore, when you see to know the color of the moisture, try all the surrounding quarter, because that is the form as it was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the surrounding quarter, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, then it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to our power and the fullness of his body; then cover him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit at his right side, and stretch the leg to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula left, and cut the skin of the testicles between the long one down to the pointy part, and make your incision straight in cutting the skin of the testicles just up to the white leucorrhoea, and scrape it subtly according to our power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the white leucorrhoea with water to a small pertus, and extract all the water, and then put your fingers, and stretch the white leucorrhoea upwards; and do not touch the skin of the testicles, but only the white leucorrhoea, cut it out or in pieces just as subtly, that if you do not cut it well, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg bursts forth from your work, then put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the white leucorrhoea; then gather the two leaves of the skin of the testicles into one seam, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie up the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the decoration of blood; then cut the testicle to all the suspended part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if water is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two ramices; then cut the other part similarly to what you did with the first one, then stop the blood, and put a linen cloth moistened in rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another linen cloth moistened in wine and oil, and place it over the two testicles, and put doubled cloths above, and tie it up with all the bandage that is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths and fill them with woolly material according to this shape and gather them by sewing in the girth of the breeches, and one of the straps takes hold on the foundation just up to the back, and the other at the pointed part; and the other strap goes above the two inguinal rings, and be all gathered into a bundle in the loop of the breeches.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this medicine of fire cautery is taken in place of iron surgery, and it is that you take .i. subtle cultellaire cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white scab that contains water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that scab with fine points, and scrape it off with a subtle hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut in all ways that you can, until you have removed everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more wholesome; and take care to prevent bleeding, and be mindful of the incisions.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing else makes you contrary, or abscesses or bleeding or anything else, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horribleness, then administer perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs that we have said that the fire has taken hold,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	so sit the patient on a soft couch; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the entire spacious area, and place the perforation along the length of the body; and make the holes large, so that all the water can flow forth.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and let the remaining water flow forth, then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not allow water to come out of the wound mouth, then it is necessary that you put in a probe or instrument used for draining the waters of dropsy, as we have described before; and enlarge one pore of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after seven months or so around, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this remedy there are more fears and dispositions, therefore it seems to me that one should not leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and indeed to the testicles; and this is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know that it comes from bitter superfluity and ague, which spreads to the testicles, or from percussion.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not find pain, and is a grievous abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance is a grievous and pesky abscess, of foul color, and sometimes comes from no artery or from swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to no artery, then it is known by the disposition of hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not seem right that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made of swelling of the vein is known by its disposition to expression through the feeling of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can do well with surgery on this likeness and on other bodies.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the skin of the testicles, then lift the egg upwards and scrape off the white scab, and deliver the suspended matter from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already sodden with these bodies, then it is necessary that you scrape off the egg and the skin.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is stuck to the scab or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that mass and cut it again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the lump is in the back part, then it is necessary that you cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then apply the wound with wet wool in rose oil and wine, and then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bunchberry, with the softening of the testicles,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the patient grows gravely ill when they walk.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure for this disease is just as frightening as the one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a soft couch, then put the suspensory of the testicles down to your fingers.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near the penis, and tie them in place with the master's strings, and stretch them out properly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut at the spacious area cutting a wide traverse around the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape off from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are on the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle where there is a doubled thread, and tie it to the first place where the blood came out, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them straight in the middle, according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupted moistures.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then cure the wound as with others that are inflamed, so that no vessel may bleed that would nourish one of the testicles.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels come forth blood, then it is necessary to drain the testicles from all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the testicles do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and wither and are unable to be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the scab
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The effects of this remedy are by the section that comes from the scab, or the extension above the belly in the part of the inguinal region, therefore the intestines descend through that rupture to one of the testicles.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either from the scab or from the extension of it, and comes in two ways by many causes: either by percussion, or by jump, or by bray, or by lifting a heavy weight, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the scab are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal up to the very bottom, because the scab presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the scab, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear in diverse forms, just below the skin, and this is because of the issue of the intestine and the body's departure through the scab.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the umbilicus, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, wherefore one should avoid them with fear.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to bring his intestines back to their place within the wound, if he can reach it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be stretched over his neck between your hands, and lift up his shoulders.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the skin above, and cut off all the fat from the length of the scrotum.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push inside the leaves of the flaps according to what you need to open the wound, and make them such that the opening can emerge.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then flay the scrotum that is beneath the skin of the scrotum, until the white scrotal membrane is uncovered from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then place your two fingers in the part that separates the scrotum, between the white scrotal membrane which is beneath the skin of the testicle and between the second scrotal membrane.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and separate what is behind the testicle, and between the second scrotal membrane; and then move your hand to the right within the skin of the scrotum, and stretch the white scrotal membrane upwards to your left hand, and lift the testicle away from all the scrotal tissue towards the thigh.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle upwards and release what is above behind the bond.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and search with your two fingers if the intestine has enveloped or wrapped around the white scrotal membrane, and if you find anything, then put it into the belly beneath.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle with which there is one thick thread made of ten threads, and put it in the rear part of the scrotum, which is after the skin of the scrotum; after the thigh, then cut off the knots that appear from the threads, until there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then gather them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the scrotum, which we have said is beneath the skin of the scrotum, with a strong bond of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the knots of the threads and tie them together with a bond of two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter in there, lest an abscess should not arise.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the band on top according to the first bond long with two fingers of that one, and after these two bands leave the scrotum which is beneath the skin of the scrotum a quarter of an inch.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that the other according to the roundness that the testicle bears; then cut in the part which is beneath the skin of the scrotum, until the cord and the bow are like we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply moist wool in oil to the wounds, and put on it the band that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white scrotal membrane that we have said is cauterized after incision, due to fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and leave the band until it falls off by itself; and if it takes too long to fall off, then raise it with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia of flesh
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy I never saw anyone who dared to make the treatment by fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones say that it is done in the same way as the remedy that is together with the life, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the thigh on the underside lightly.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut it in half and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels cease; and then cure it as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes the bowels come out in anger, as we have said, and open the gut; and none of the intestines descend to the scrotum, and if any do, it is rare, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and yet if he stays too long in this position, the wound or scrotal membrane will grow, until the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the scrotal membrane which is at the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and inflated the gut and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is done by cauterization, as we have said before; and sometimes it is not cured by iron in this way.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies sovient on his back between your hands, then cut the gut of the hernia inflated to its width according to the quantity of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the scrotal membrane that is beneath the skin which follows it, and take the rim and put it on top of the gut apparent from the scrotal membrane.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the bottom of the belly, then cut the two guts apparent from the scrotal membrane on top of the rim, and cut one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the rim, and do not cut the scrotal membrane or stretch the testicle nor any other thing, as I have made known to you in the treatment of the remedy for the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the threads, so that the patient may not be troubled and cure the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scrotal membrane is constricted, and has no appearance in the hernia, and the cauterization is more fruitful in this wound, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum is softened in some men, because the contents that are inside are softened, and it is to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on his back, and cut off the soft skin above the natural skin; then gather the two lips together into a seam, and if you see, cut off first the superfluous part of the softened skin at three or four seams; then cut between the seams, and treat it as one would other wounds, until he is healed, and the thread falls away.
dou chastrement	of correction or punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	I know that correction is ordained in our law, and so it pleases me that I should not speak of it at all in this book. And it is only necessary for two purposes: one is that the physician may answer when asked about a remedy and its cure; and the other is because we often have need to correct certain beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Des hermofrodites is according to two manners of men: the one manner is when between the two testicles it appears as much as the figure of a woman's nature, and there is hair, and sometimes in court the urine flows. And the other manner is in women, and has above the finger as much as a rod and two testicles. And the cure for men and women is that you close the torn parts together and care for it as for other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tentigenous.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».
