Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigenous is a torn part above the natural part, as much as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the cure. It is necessary that you dye the excess of the tentigenous with your hand or fingers, and close it lightly; and do not go too deeply into it, lest blood flow from it, then treat another wound until it is healed; and to another part that arises at the mouth of the womb, and fills, and by chance jumps forward, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and therefore they called it in olden times "cow disease". It is necessary that you close it as we have said the tentigenous, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of the erratic.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the womb is small; and it is caused by birth or accident due to disease that has occurred; or it's because of a torn part or subtle abscess, and it makes a hole in the womb, sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and even having flowers (i.e., menstruation); and the knowledge of this is determined by gazing at the belly. If the abscess is close to appearing, it will go to your right or left. If it's a subtle abscess, and it's close to the two kidneys, hasten and do thus: place your two fingers together, and the woman be on her back with her legs spread; then press the two kidneys firmly until the subtle abscess is gone, and cover the abscess with a cloth; then have the woman lie down each day, so that it cannot coalesce. And if the abscess is hard and coarse, you must cut it off in a manner resembling a myrtle leaf. If the abscess is of natural flesh, suspend it at the oncus and close it; and use medicines stopping blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and eggshell, together with many other remedies; then administer a broad belt of linen, so that the wound cannot coalesce; and thus be treated for a long time, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured of other wounds until it is healed. And when in the womb comes natural flesh, you must close it according to this manner, unless it's an enchanted aposteme. For an enchanted aposteme that is in the womb, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which, without corticization, become accustomed; and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division their likenesses, signs, and I will say here those that receive a cure. I say that hemorrhoids and hardened things, when they are deeply seated in the womb, and there is no sensation, it is not cured by fire. Those that are at the mouth of the womb, where one can feel them, are those that one can cure. It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then place the hardened thing on tongs, and close it in its roots, then powder with medicines restraining blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then dip her feet in cold water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes from it, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomace skin and galls, and similar things; and then take barley flour, mix with honey and oil, and make one plaster on her back. And if it subsides, that is good. If not, make poultices on the back and breasts to avoid further irritation; then take linen, moisten in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply to the wound. And when the aposteme recedes, cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a rough head, so close it as I said for hardened things; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of the apostemes of the womb.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Here is the translation of the text:
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary first at the delivery that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and signs if you see her hastening downward, and desiring to give birth; then the infant hastens to emerge forth; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is beneath its head, and the secondine with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the infant emerges soon; for when it descends above its head, the secondine is with it, and the midwife removes excess fluids by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes beneath its feet, or above its body or legs, or hand, or on its belly, or under; and it is converted by chance to its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant emerges above its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth grievously, and her virtues are weak, then make her sit on a stool, or have the women hold her; and arise her nature from oil or fenugreekic be cooked, and then pour the balm between her breasts the small spatula-like thing which is its shape.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the secondine, and compress it to its umbilical cord as long as the moistors that are enclosed force; and take hold of the woman's belly until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to purge the woman with fenugreek mucilage mixed with sesame oil; then make her press and evacuate her condisi, and keep her mouth and nose shut for an hour: thus the infant has emerged. And if the two hands emerge forth, then it is necessary that you gently draw them out bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then set the stool back down on the ground, and support the woman so she does not fall while getting up; and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant has died, then compress the hands to the cutting tool that is placed before this, and extract the child, and draw it out evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From childbirth of the infant on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant emerges on its feet, it is necessary to lift it up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it bit by bit until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can't he just jump up to his hips, if she commands him to press, and make her evacuate her condisi.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he jumps out, as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he is not forth as we have said, then turn him bit by bit until he is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is so slightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if he does not come forth as we have said, then take fenugreek mucilage, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put it on the woman's nature inside and outside with this ointment.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in warm water up to the armpits.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened below, make a collar of myrrh and put it on her, and let her wear it for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a stool, then make her evacuate and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the infant is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From childbirth of the infant on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this form, then put the balm on his hands bit by bit.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then be gentle on its neck, and let the feet hang down below, and be placed on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands bit by bit, and then press the hands on her belly, and remove the cushions below, until she is prepared downward.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the infant does not jump, then take its feet and fold them gently, then fold the belly upwards, then put your hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and ease the infant bit by bit; and command the woman to take hold until the infant emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From childbirth of the infant which emerges with one arm stretched out
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to ingeniously bring back the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on a bed, and gently loosen her legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the mucilage that I have told.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a stool, and study how to bring back the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and ease the infant according to its natural shape, and make her evacuate, and command her to take hold until the infant emerges forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From childbirth of the infant on its neck, with spread arms and face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the balm holds its hand, then turn it bit by bit, and ease it slightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then put on the natural mucilage of fenugreek and oil, as we have said, and command her to move bit by bit.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then make her sit on a stool, and command her to take hold; and make her evacuate.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner for all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this way to all the secondine, then compress the secondine with your finger, until the moistors is emptied.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the infant puts its face and neck on it, then compress from below, so that it is not retained, and kill the infant.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the infant inside, as long as you have placed it as is necessary, and command the woman to take hold sometimes:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then it will be so slightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	From childbirth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born sometimes, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens bit by bit.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live unless they have a name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are torn apart by the cord that divides them, which is tied to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out naturally as one below, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are grievous, then the cure as we have said, and be the bail subtle, and do soon and lightly what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is worth for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb, that is to say, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, and up to fifteen, and all are shaped in the form of an infant by the measurement of divine wisdom.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the bail knows all this, for similar things may happen to him by chance;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do as it is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman after giving birth to a dead child or stillbirth, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to do manual work;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fears death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be positioned on her back, and have her head inclined downwards, and her legs lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife takes hold of two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she will not be moved down from the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then wipe the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the bail's hands with these oils and mixtures;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then pour them into the womb lightly, then take one or two of those leaves that are suitable for this purpose;
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care to see if the child is descended onto its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you place the leaves in his eyes or on his neck or in his mouth or on his palate or under the beard or in the forehead or near the ribs;
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is onto feet, then place it or prick it and cut off the moles;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the leaf in his right hand, and puts the cord between his left thighs, and pours it all over his hand lightly, and places the leaf in any of those leaves that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the leaf;
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then place it against another leaf, or the third one you have need of, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other, so that the leaves are bent, in order for them to stay, as this is the form;
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then anoint some of the bail's fingers with oil and pour it into that part, and treat the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if none remains, then place this leaf or higher one, and do so until it comes out entirely;
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot return because of the constriction;
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	so it is necessary that you wrap it on one cloth, until it comes out entirely;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then bind it at the joint of the plant or at the cut, and thus it is necessary that you do so in the other hand, and have two feet;
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is thin in the issue, or it has a sharp-pointed head assembled;
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	so it is necessary that you pour the spine-bone between your thighs, and bend the head and extract the water;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you cut it with the instrument which is called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and do so likewise if the child has a large natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pull out the bones with forceps;
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps forward and it is strained at the forehead, so that it is split, until the moisture that is in the birth issue flows;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you make a hole until the moisture runs;
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the movement is light, and the directing to the mouth of the womb is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is thin in the belly or at the breast, then it is necessary that you extract it to one cloth wrapped on the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and open the belly or breast, until the moisture that is there runs;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are broken off, and the head remains;
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	so the bail pours his hand into the birth canal, and pulls it up to the mouth of the womb;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then pour in one or two leaves, and pull it out;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the womb is constricted because of a hot abscess that has come there, then it is not necessary to work at all;
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	rather it is necessary to prepare moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the applier applies unguents, and puts in softening and moistening waters.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it equal, then apply what we have said in a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot, then pull it out by pieces, and leave nothing of the remaining part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, apply what we have said in hot abscesses that come into the womb;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding comes from the womb, then it should be put in restraining water, and the applier should apply other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose child had been dead in the womb, then she consulted another doctor on top of that, and the other doctor rejected the dead one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to the mouth of the womb, and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to cause great disturbance.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied an ointment of strong attraction, and one bone came out, and after some days another did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very astonished, because the womb has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I treated the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived for a long time like that, and every now and then she would pass a little bit of blood from her loins.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not read this chapter except that when the master finds a strange thing, he should know how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the joint back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of the preserver, by which we preserve books; and at the second turning to the second joint of the two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the corners should be more subtle than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the wood should be one and a half palms wide, and the edge of the trees one palm, and long a palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two lines should be two joints of this same wood, which are firm on one and the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joints are inserted in the mouth of the joint so that it can be opened when one turns the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, even more subtle and light, should be made of wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of pincers;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two joints, two hinges, as you see, one palm long and one and a half palms wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the joint open to all the instrument, then make the woman sit on one litter, with her feet bent and her legs outstretched,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two hinges together in the joint, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the entire instrument, just as you have done with pincers evenly, according to the amount that you see the mouth of the joint open, until the patient makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted, and their shapes are multiplied; and when the makers have prepared them, then is the work more hasty, and higher in price for men according to their quality.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, then you should instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her exhale slowly, and hold your hands on the mouth and navel;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she coughs for that reason, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take one pot, and make one perforation or cover, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the joint, such as chamomile, rue, anise, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs or some of them should be cooked or put in water on the fire; then put one end of the pot and the other head into the mouth of the joint.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it stay until the vapors come inside the joint; then make her exhale, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine comes forth quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and is not fully cured, instruct the patient to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or mullein juice from hawthorn, and then put it in its natural state.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and the secondine will come out; and when she has found it, then take hold of it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the joint does not hinder its extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it is necessary to move it slightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; and it will come out and be dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the joint is narrow, we have said the treatment for exhaling and the fumigation of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not cured by all that we have said, then beware that you do not force the extraction.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the joint, you tie to the woman's groin, then anoint her with ointment of fourfold physician.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	and it will help and restore her, and she will come forth; but nevertheless, when she has purged in this way, a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to make suitable fumigations for this: none of the ancients have proven that fumigation with cress and dried figs is effective.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument by which one fumes the woman at the retention of flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it looks like a cord, and one puts the head into nature, and the wide ends above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and let it stay until it is spent, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced, but rather it has been stopped by a subtle syphilis.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary for the patient to pierce that syphilis at its tip, and not pierce with sharp spatula, and guard the ligament so she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist linen cloth in wine and oil, then the treatment with ointment until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not close, then put or make a perforation in a piece of cloth, and let it stay for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And whenever this swelling comes from sudden wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cover that swelling: then be cured, as we have said of the cloth wrapping.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodulations, and grow larger as they come from the sides of the foundation or in the space between the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	and if there is one or more fistulas; and when that nodulation is old, it opens up, and then makes more moisture, white or subtle pus.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are purulent; and they are known by this that there is or ejection or evacuation when the patient makes ejection, and by chance jumps out one or two verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and they reach just to the groin junction, and just to the top of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the purulent fistula at the foundation, and not the non-purulent one.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your two indices or foundation, and insert a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuousness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, then bind with a thin cloth or one hair of a horse, as long as you feel the cloth or hair at your touch.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and there is no emission of pus, wind, or urine, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not puncture; if the wound hastens to heal.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is piercing just to the bladder or just to the channel of urine, if the urine jumps out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just to the jointure of the hip, then the tent is coming just to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the cause of the pain around it, then it is that he goes down to the bowels, and it is not worth medicine or a poultice by anointing.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these piercing fistulas there is no cure except for labor, and the vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not piercing and not ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then bind a cloth of linen or of wool if there is tortuosity, as long as you know where the cloth comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around his fundament, then it is necessary that you apply your two fingers to it.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then sense that the cloth has pierced it; and be discovered where you feel between your skin or flesh, then know that it is piercing.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not labor on it, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says however that one can well heal some, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that one makes there, is to burn the small cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and bind it all hot in the fistula, until it comes to the fundament; and make this twice or three times, as long as you know that those burnt char pieces are like a feather of a bird.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moist cloths in butter, until that burnt char comes out; then cure it with anointing oil pouring and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is healed thus, it is well. If not, otherwise he cannot be healed.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the cloth enters and does not pierce just to the skin which is on the fundament, and there is between your two fingers and the cloth a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula at that point where the covering of the flesh begins.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	so cut from the beginning of the fistula and bind afterwards before the cloth, and then burn with a cautery until it comes to the top of the cloth.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the cloth will be delivered and fall off; then remove those burnt char pieces that resemble a feather of a bird, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood vainly swells and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine as needed.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For fire cauterizes two good things: that is to say, the burning of those charred pieces, and the staunching of blood and the drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then cure it with moist cloths in butter or in a broken eggshell, as long as the wound pours bile, and let the burnt char pieces come out into the bowel.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound with anointing oils that bind and dry hard flesh, and are the medicines dried up.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the very bottom of the fundament, and is removed from the body, then bind your two fingers or fundament, and inspect it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the cloth, and between two is the thread or skin or flesh, where it is close to piercing, then there should be no other remedy except for the way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you burn it as we have said, or cut it just to the foundation, or if you can, put cloths and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far down into the foundation, lest you cut the dwelling that holds the fundament, and come forth with excrement unwillingly.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it as soon as it is cut below the fundament, by cloth or by another instrument appointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then remove that burnt flesh piece which is in the wound, as long as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And there are no fistulas according to this manner: and is when you bind the cloth in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament below the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	so take a pierced cloth at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I bind one twisted thread into two, and bind the cloth to all the thread in the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is piercing within the margin of the fundament inside, then take out the thread from that hole, so that you bind your two fingers or fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull the top of the thread, and gather the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it remain for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it at no time, until the thread cuts those charred pieces that are between two, and they fall away.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is bound up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too far down.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not good to make a hole cut so deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spine-like espinous from which one makes the fistula is much rougher in one part and torn.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other part not, therefore one should not cut what one should not cut, as you see here.
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: or they are inside the fundament, like a small piece of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in cutting away blood flows.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if there is one or more, and they are without foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are without it have little moisture
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and then a little bit of yellow water or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the flesh
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them inside the foundation is that you instruct the patient to lie down in chambers until the foundations come forth, and then the sons appear
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	so hasten, and hold it with pincers, or you hold it to your finger, then cut at its roots
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the bandages cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take one of linen, or cotton, or a piece of camlet
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them from your hands, then cut, and powder with some hot powders that are in place of cauterization
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize as it is said or written in the chapter on cauterization, then treat with other treatments until they are healed
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then purgative him with a bitter and sharp clyster to cleanse what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient is well prepared, and if the sons are out of the foundation, then the treatment is gentle
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them in your finger or with pincers, and cut, then treat as we have said, until he is healed, and so that he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you sew according to this manner: take one twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of the width; and bind the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for closing the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation one moistened linen cloth in rose oil or cerotin, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave him until he has relieved himself, and when they have ceased, treat with ointment and other treatments until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the suppuration of the wound or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is suppuration of wounds in the intestine, and due to natural constraint, and when the patient is old and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you remove the scab on top with a spatula or your finger, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is sound as it is necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before until it heals thoroughly and is scraped off.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formication is a small, failed appearance on the skin, and it goes very deeply in.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the frost takes hold of him, and it is felt all over like death from formication, and comes to hands more than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose or a strong turkey's feather, and put that quill on the formication, until the circles surround the formication entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the entire quill until you cut all around the formication, and put it deeply in, and extract the formication from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then make those of a copper or iron quill according to this form, and be subtle beneath and trailing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not to pierce, but to keep it at the two and to press; And if you see, then cauterize the formication, as is written or said in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or archaute, or melted and malleable copper; and sometimes one makes those small and great instruments, according to the way they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then which are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and great clyster is above large, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an opening or the belly is tied as you see, and the channels inside pierced; and have two holes on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly or stomach is where you put medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have between each hole one thread of espace, then put in these holes one strong thread of twisted thread in ten or eleven parts around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it with the instrument before with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk or similar thing, then put it in gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then have the attendants press with their two hands together until it is all visible, then extract the clyster, and lift the patient's legs to the sight.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine needs to come out, then let it stay as long as it can; and if he sleeps one whole night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize in the disease of windiness of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as many times as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the foundation or abscess, then be the clyster as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster above which the skin will be strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; and now we will say the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or with lance or stick or seat, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	wherein are done according to the places of the body, as wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head simple, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to a stone or similar things, and the skin is all torn and the wound is great.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt slightly of an abscess hot: if you make it heal soon by the cephalic way itself even if it comes out with blood from the wound, and let the healing be contrary to the damaged part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to fill up on wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not want to heal, so be it reduced its meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound if an abscess hot comes, a moist cloth in rose oil alone, or in vinegary wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound powder which I will say soon after.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the ulcer has been moved by fire, then put on some unguents until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stretching, then bring them together by stitching, just as I will say about belly wounds by stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered of bone and greenish and barely holds together by a thread, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as cooked testicles and wheat, also like pigeons, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find putrid flesh and it is not attached to the bone, then cut out all the putrid part and throw it away, then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stanched by medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it severed, then bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put this powder which unites just as much as fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live coal, and grind the powder subtly,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it closes well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coal alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but only if fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if fire has moved the wound, especially in this state, then do not put one ounce of this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive unguents, or pigeons made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it flows freely.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone break comes with the wound, and it is small, then set it with fine tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you soon after about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between that and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, like charcoal washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and let it wash also in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of my mine according to this manner, and moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, then bind it with cloth and tie with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and full of pus, then puncture or cut below it.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and blood comes out, then dissect it, and tie it, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the gullet, and the conduit is preserved, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	so cut the gullet on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it gently, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then cut it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then treat them all as you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound putrefies.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be separated and cleansed the discharge.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a cut from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are any signs of inflammation around the wound that the patient complains of: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder in the wound at first hour, nor bind it for the blood that does not clot in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and rekindles in the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on attractive ointment, and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have balm, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on top of the wound three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no convulsion, nor ill trembling in the heart nor drawing out of tendons;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with tents and other treatments, until he is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if she cannot heal, nor open, then know that there is a fistula; and cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or deeper or on the back, then cure what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, then close the wound, and remove the pus if it is open.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not open, then let the wound suppurate, so that the extractions will ease.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes a portion of the intestine or one of the intestinal loops bursts open, by which there is an entrance for them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a great one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	therefore it is better to put the intestines back in gradually, rather than all at once.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell soon as they feel cold, and thus enter more slowly.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to make the wound smaller, because one should put the intestine back in its place that belongs to the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and the two other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine protrudes,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if something is to be put back, it is done by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one piece of cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or boil it in water with aqua sanguinis, and cypress, and spikenard,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and apply the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine restrains and is good to ease swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or boil it with malva and mallow.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this it is eased the entrance to receive a little something;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument used to cut off hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is better than the cutting,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that one should not cut without great necessity or need.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to divide:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside the curvature and do not cut too far, and see where the shape is.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its natural place according to its proper location.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can manage, for this is better.
