Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and breasts higher than the lower parts.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then put your attention on making the injured part higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to manage what I say about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds put what is appointed to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands one pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound one or two fingers' breadth, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the siphac,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is underneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the siphac to form a triple knot;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a double thread around the needle on both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and bring together the two sides of the wound in a natural way,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one or two fingers' breadth, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this according to your need for needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles moderate, between fine and coarse.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot enter well at all:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary for them to be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	lest they cut and open the wound before the suturing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles, so that they do not disturb the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and put tents or cloths on the ends of the needles to hold them in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them so until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it can be done with one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching if is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two pieces of leather and the two pieces of silk together with a needle where there is one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these pieces all four together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then tie the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitching, the thickness of a minor denier;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching is good for men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that a man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width deep,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were exposed two palms' width deep,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestines and he had been without them for 24 hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was closed in just 15 days, and I healed it, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I didn't anoint him with ointment, because I was in one place where you couldn't find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I placed clean cotton cloth over the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it through from the outside to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the corner of right in right, then tie off the end of the silk or thread where you put in the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side into the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the intention of this stitching is that you sew as pelt makers make their pelts,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the silk on one side and then take it up again on the other, until the stitching is all finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galen says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like those who assemble the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the silk to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	push a needle or hook close by, and make it pierce that point alone,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the silk;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside to the inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	like two ends of silk;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside, in two other hooks that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says that this word, and some testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew corsets;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when a rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, and the air has made it turn;
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestines and the gut; then apply powder of burnt charcoal on top,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the air has made it turn, then apply some ointment that is present until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and tie off the silk and the needle;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then apply, at first, clean cotton cloth;
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it two times a day until he is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in many simple wound cases;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound may cause community among the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is good that you moisten linen lightly with temperate heat oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the groins and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or itching in his bowels, and this often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then they should be cleansed with black wine tea, and likewise if the itching comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and probe inside, and knows that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily healed than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is due to the thickness of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the approach of its nature to that of swine.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts forth from the wound, then put it back in place just as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it has turned yellow or black, then it is good that you tie up the part that is black, so that no bleeding comes from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two ends hanging from the part below the wound to the outside in order to ease the extraction when the intestines fall out and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	then it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and it was the wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became gangrened and turned into a fistula, and from there came the evacuation and the flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the flesh had closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the patient did not have an illness in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no illness, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced people say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh linen from large sheets, then close the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the linen has covered the mouth, put it on top of the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth over;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then bind the head, and this will hold so he cannot loosen.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put one more piece of linen after in that same way as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This method will heal in the intestine and cause no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread that is sewn from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this thread of intestine that is well cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie at the end of this thread one thin piece of linen twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then thread the thread onto a needle, and sew the intestine, and tie it in the bowstring;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with linen is not other than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestine, there is no remedy or health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it is cut and flows down.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the true nodation, hard and white, or one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it flows like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear liquid flow, and other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and has no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing but due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the lips, that does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much liquid;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the lump is rotten, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in the region it is slow to digest, and delays health, and flows naturally by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistula which is made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the bladder, or intestine, or bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar lumps.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come just to the point I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it recognized, then take a piece of iron or clay, if the fistula is straight, and cut;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a thin piece of flint;
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the flint bends to conform to the twisting shape.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	so cleanse it through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one opening to another, and purifies it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then cut it off at your discretion, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it flows out in abundance,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you, then sew according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and take away the rotten flesh and corrupt matter that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then continue to treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well opened at the right place, then it is necessary that you sew in abundance as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist tents of medicinal water and tie them just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put on gentle ointments of healthy flesh, until it is cleansed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not injure you or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it away until all the corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with gentle things to promote healthy flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and flows again as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the end.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	so uncover and cut until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to approach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy than to rely on nature's help.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can extract it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many moles, so treat them all, nor leave any one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes you contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	so mix and moisten and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, so place on the wound something fermenting and rotting.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will be easier to remove;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a great bone, such as of thigh or hip,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	so remove only the corruption until all the marrow is removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corrupted flesh, and it comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so scrape and clean all up to the corruption, and then care for it until it is closed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in someone's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so much so that the materials came to the leg, and it was filled with a great abscess, and there was no reason to fail to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctors by their foolishness opened so much that the abscess burst open,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a great many materials were flowing out, and it became a fistula, and there came out very much pus that all flowed forth with bad smell and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many doctors put treatment around 2 years, and there was no remedy in their skill of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed out through the pus was very foul.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the skin of the young man became red and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a tent in one of these pus-filled sores, and then searched all the pus-filled sores,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some came together with others from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and scraped in one of the pus-filled sores until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came just to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be from the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for what I had removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicines according to the passage of long time, and could not close;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then recommenced, and found the bone just as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then took it away, and waited to close the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I scraped around a palm's length of the bone, and removed it to its very marrow,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then restored it with medicines; and he was healed and closed quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through evacuation it often bled, but he was healed entirely,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and instead of the bone a hard flesh arose, and he was in good condition and had no harm or contradiction from anything at all, neither to go nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, then it must be scraped in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one linen cloth, and stretch it over the top of the exposed bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to hold it up high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place one other linen cloth, larger than the first one, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top, so that you remove the corrupt flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the place where you see to scrape, so that the scraping does not wound the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a wooden spatula under the bone to move and cover the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to scrape as much as can be seen and felt of the corruption, and scrape again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh; then put a hot iron underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape from one part to the other the corruption, and be sure to scrape as far as the length of the corruption is, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then scrape the corrupted joint, and scrape the bone on one side as far as it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than to scrape;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the fingers of the hand or in the toes, then it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but all the same you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and scrapers for scraping these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the methods of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument that you need, according to what it requires.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder may be dislocated due to a cause within or due to a cause outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have made medicines for that corruption by the treatment of medicines, and they do not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	so it is necessary to scrape off that member up to the point where the corruption comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient may escape either by death or by evil, which is greater than the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are such that the members become black, as if they were burned with fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards it becomes pale, then goes that corruption from member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of everything in the body; if you hasten to cut,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is in the head of the joint, if it cuts, and does not give space for it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy against it except for the quantity of his virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so it goes when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut all the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister down one strap, and another minister up the other strap,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh between the two straps with one spatula wide, so that the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or sew, and place one linen cloth on each side, so that the sewing does not touch the healthy flesh.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and abscess breaks out in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood flows away comes when you work, then cauterize the place hastily,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in summer:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a burn that seemed like the burning of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption came first to his joint in the foot, so that it consumed all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corruption came again to the joint of his hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that were corrective after the purging of his body, but the corruption could not cease;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he begged me to cut off his hand, and I refused, for I had hope of correcting the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the virtue of the man was weak; and he became despairing, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and then hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told this story only for the reason that one may do another thing if need arises.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in fatty flesh, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, and the flesh remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as subtle as one of those delicate cloths;
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not run up to the bone, nor up to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain";
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes up to the bone in front, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is that you cut all around that skin, and similarly when it is subtle, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in front,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then clean it with a poultice like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the sinews are large, and the pus that issues from them has a foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then one must clean it with Egyptian medicine made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take aloes, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	so that the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it to cleanse the sinew, and stop the abscess;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the sinew is cleared, and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes one should clean it with ash water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and use it to cleanse, until you know that the sinew is well cleared.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then clean him with water and honey or add a little litharge to it;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or cleanse him with honey and sweet wine, which have the property of purifying and cleansing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the skin healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the sinew is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then cleanse him with what makes flesh grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and that is by taking definite plaster, and mixing it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or cleanse him with some medicines and unguents, whose properties I have described or how to treat the unguents;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the abscess of the sinew is small, and the catheter of the cleanser cannot enter it.
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	so enlarge it with a little iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilikon ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then cut and leave it so that only one point or the catheter can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the abscess that issues pus is above, then cut or lower it to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is in front, it does not allow flesh to remain;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you see
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	so it is arranged in such a way that the bow goes to its lowest place that is.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the bow is bent, it does not allow any flesh to interleave.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you see
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so it is arranged in such a way that the bow goes down slightly and does not leave anything of the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stretch it over one cloth of linen that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cover the strong spot on the breast in a pouch slightly larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then smear soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the depression,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the breast of the breast to ease the bow and not remove the great cloth until after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that one on the breast of the breast is often removed to remove the bow,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows what comes out from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough or undigested or indigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has extended in such a way that you see the nature that rises up on the breast of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then knows that the breast is healed and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning or the third day, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast ejects undigested bowel after many days, knows that the breast is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come out shortly after long time, don't despair of health at all.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because health approaches. For there are men whose flesh does not mingle well in their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowel shoots out from the breast after many days, knows that the breast is not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes long to heal and is swollen, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	just as defined ointment, for it has a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same for honey cooked thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defined ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue it onto a cloth, and stretch it over the breast, and do not administer it to an Aristologist for a long time,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of the heaven, which is also like fine wheat flour and hundredfold;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them as simples or compounds: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then knows that corruption is in its depths, and makes an impression on the bone, or hardens the members, or makes ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so treat the wound of a fistula, as we have said before this.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the joint
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Abscess is an abscess that arises beneath the joint of the little finger of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or by chance occurs in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and one does not take care, then a bad abscess comes forth,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the joint, and by chance may even go all the way around.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to corrosion right up to the bone, so that it brings a stinking pain, and the toe of the foot is wide, and the color is fiery.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so it is necessary that you remove all the excess fluid that remains from the joint,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the joint begins to putrefy the flesh, and starts to prick and bleed,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so it is necessary that you place the thread under the joint where the flesh is pricked,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up above, and remove that subtle and delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then remove it, and treat the wound, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it will not heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the toe corrupting, then remove it in one of the ways mentioned above as it was said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the joint of the spatula in a diagonal direction above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not come down to the flesh which is below the joint, for the patient would feel too great a pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The toes that occur in some men's hands by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is one or two where there are bones, and sometimes there is a joint.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or birth in some of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	That which is born in any of the nails of the toe does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and that which is born at the joint of the toe, by chance moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of one who is fleshy is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: if you take it to be cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In that which is born or grows on the back of the toe, it is necessary that you remove the flesh around to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cover the bone with a suitable thread to it, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come together come by birth, or by sudden wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you cover the swelling, then let it be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or moistened cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his hands with the palm, then cover that swelling as it should be.
Des vils	The vile(s)
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are swollen, large, and full of superfluous melancholy things that come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it is more frequent in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him occasional purging with vinegar, and then heal with the oil of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron remedy is according to two manners: one is when you cover it, and then tie up the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein, and let all the blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is according to this manner: first arise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned out,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two places, or three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and let flow the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood has flowed out as the patient's virtue can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command that he abstain from meat, drinking black vinegar;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and healing when the veins are clean, and it is good for the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The shaving of him is according to this manner: rise the patient's leg if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and arise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat him by the fire, and then cut in the direction of the vein from long to short at the top of the kneecap, or in the part below to the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply the leather to the inflammation, and scrape off the vein from each side, until it appears when you touch it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the leather it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the end down below, until it is lifted from the leather, and then bend it to the inflammation slightly;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut in another place above three fingers; then scrape off the leather on the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up to the fold, just as you did, and bend it to another inflammation, just as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if you need it, then lift it, and cut to the toe of the foot;
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then let it flow and lift up to the second incision; then pull it from incision to incision, until it flows all out, then cut;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot make it flow and lift, then insert a needle into each strong thread doubled,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and let it flow, and insert below one end, and turn your hand from side to side, until it flows out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and take care that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then one cannot make it flow or lift, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have let it all flow out, then put moist wool on the wound in wine and rose oil; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut it crosswise, but do not cover it; and let it flow as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut straight, so that it cuts the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the Civil Vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is situated in legs, in hot places where there are no herbs or tree, and on earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be located in another place besides the leg, and this happens because of the purulence that comes from beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if a serpent or worm were to come forth within the body, and then twist between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg with a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the skin changes and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the abscess opens, then it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth one and a half inches to two and a half inches, and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it starts to open up again, wrap it around the cloth, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it has come out entirely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring about abscess and purulence at the wound, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that she be treated gradually from top to bottom, and that nothing remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when it is treated with five or ten inches,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it issued from ten inches of length, and when you cut it, he put in one end or a pucker, and pierces all the way to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all comes out; and the matter inside be emptied, and administer to the wound medicines which prevent purulence for some days, then care for it as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes at this vein many streams come out, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or on the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes much pus, and it bursts forth; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	There are worms that come between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "beef disease", because it often affects oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and it goes up and down through all the body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he feels it well as it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it goes and bursts forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is filled with various purgings of some humors, such as come from worms, serpents, and lice or roundworms in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its maliciousness, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot avoid it except when it is being removed:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you bind the area above and below with a strong tie tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and pull it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire above until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it damages the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye at the top of the head, then bind below it with a band tightly, then cut above and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient in a purging of the body with soluble medicines for the bad humors produced.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and warn him against eating foods that produce purging.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windy distension.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rising like a worm on the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	even sooner than anything else, just as sharp silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then soon after it ran throughout the body until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body again, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease move like that before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many who had been known to have pain move from one place to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it like that, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought to myself that it was because the woman had a dry body and her veins were uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore appeared the windy distension constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason to those who are delighted and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then bind above and below quickly, and then cut above until the constrained windy distension is pulled out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat it with those things that resist windy distension, such as fetid pills and serpentine pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and those with hair-like projections, and those with rivets.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two angles, and of those that have tongues, and of those which have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that falls in any member falls in two ways: either in the principal member it beheads,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you next appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary that you warn yourself against extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many conditions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and the sac that is above the brain bursts forth.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	There is when there is blindness and swelling and inflammation and redness in the eyes, and burning of the tongue, and spasms and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without force in the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it impairs speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and bursts forth from the moist white wound resembling pimples, and also bursts forth like a bruise in the flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold off on treatment and pull out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hits the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow becomes still like a pimple, and discharges black blood, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death is impending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not leave the spleen is when without foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and breathes high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the covering of the liver, it is below the small ribs; and it vomits great gall and great pain and breathes hard; and all the muscles of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food bursts forth from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and bursts forth a piece of feces through the intestine's route, there is no hope for cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the face and shoulders and neck and shoulder and aid of the back and spine and coccyx and heel and legs, and similar members, are safe according to several conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man whose arrow fell into the eye socket in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it and pulled it out on the other side of the fatty earlobe, and he was healed without any numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye under the parchment.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck, and I could only pull it out as far as the point towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, all light iron without ears; the joint was healed, and no evil accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I extracted the barbs, and softened it to the point where I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from a certain man who had been hit in the belly, and thought that he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after 30 days, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out, and there was no evil accident.
