Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a certain man to whom an arrow fell on the back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man to whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained like that without suffering great pain; and many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from a certain prince of the king, who had been hit in the nose.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely stuck.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the wound three days after it was struck. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with a fine and delicate touch, and did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on his arm an ointment attracting and digesting, because the swelling did not increase.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I found the arrow's point.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the ointment every day, and the wound healed above again, and the patient remained thus for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me that.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicinal ointment corroding by the hand every day, until it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to pull it out, and felt the head of the arrow which was lodged in the wound.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pressed into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it went across well in terms around three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then the wound opened up so that I inserted pincers, and pulled it apart from one side and the other, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop subtlety and manipulating with various instruments, until I grasped it one day with well-made pincers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of pulling out some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your treatment on what I do not say, for books cannot grasp everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters consider very little, and that which is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	and nine works, and nine instruments, for the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of members where they are stuck except by two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or from the other side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out on the side where it enters is an arrow entering soft flesh and jumping out at times.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump now, then leave it until the flesh is purged around, and the exit is cleared.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it's stuck in bone and can't come out, then leave it like that for some days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it doesn't jump, then pierce around with all subtle force, until the flesh around is stretched, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just up to one of the ventricles of the brain.
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said may happen to the patient: if you don't pull it out, but leave it until it is equal after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just up to the sacral vertebra, that's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come just up to the sacral vertebra,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without evil accident, then extracts it by pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very deeply and cannot come out at all, then administer poultices around, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, then search for it with all diligence.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowing of the wound and the depth of the arrow.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone nor nerve nor vein, so the flesh must grow until the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it clings;
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you remove the flesh that is stuck between two parts until you can move;
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then leave it until the flesh around is rotten, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flowing of blood makes you unwilling, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and think how you can pull out the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him;
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then do as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, or it reveals something about the inside, or the skin is swollen in front so that one can see or feel unpleasantly;
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for now, and then resume the extraction until it comes out forth;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is stuck, then push it all the way in.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the head breaks off, and you see that administration is needed, then administer one instrument carefully,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the edge of the instrument; and then push forth.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is broken, then insert one instrument with an entering point into it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it deserves.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the back, belly, bladder, or ribcage, and it is nearby, and you can cut above, then cut;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and nerve, and then pull it out, and then cut the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which we treat arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: great, small, and little, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the cutting instrument is also like the feather of a bird;
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push at the point of the arrow, as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for knowing if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins through which one purges are 31, from which there are 16 at the head;
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two jugular veins that are after the ears, which are called "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the back of the head;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins through which one purges commonly are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left shoulder, and people commonly call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people commonly call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right shoulder.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people commonly call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the scrotum,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one through which one purges, which appears clearly above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphena vein is the one that is between the wrist and ankle, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the fold of the pocket of the left shoulder,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphena which is at the ankle of the right shoulder; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The purging of the veins that are after the ears thus helps ancient cathartics and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the purger, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with one turn,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent loops from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then goes to your side, and where you feel the pulse under your armpit, then pinch it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and push it below the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand all the way along the vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and open the skin and vein well two fingers' breadth across, and let out as much blood as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then stop it and bind, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The purging of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for ancient migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and for headaches, and accustomed to swollen eyes, and for the body of aged tears in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the purger are thus as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the hairs below thy skin, and then signs to proceed;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the key above the vein on high at thy finger's indication, and put the lancet below,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein on high, and cut it, just as you have done in two other veins, and make the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put thy finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it strongly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their cutting and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the forehead vein is worth as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraine, and in headaches;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and put the point on the vein, and strike with thy hand or other thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that thou seest;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and no more than a slight inflammation.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good that the inflammation be too great; and the vein heals across, for the bone is near, and by chance breaks the inflammation when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the two eye sockets helps those who have the plague, and the itch, and the headache, and the yellow jaundice in the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting at some joint, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then it heals, and the bleeding from the crossing is one pace long and one pace wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the inflammation is subtle, it may break; then make the blood flow, until you need it to stop, and then bind with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding from the navel vein is worth for ague, and for feverishness, and for diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as migraine and headache that comes to the face, and similarly when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient stretches his neck, then strains his navel to thy left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle inflammation long, and put it in the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far in depth, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is soon restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the form of the inflammation:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding from the two femoral veins helps with the constriction of the gullet, and with the beginning of menstruation, and with many diseases, and with epilepsy, and with ulcers, and with boils;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient stretches his neck above one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then make the vein of the long one flow a little widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other side on the other vein, then loosen the bond, and stretch the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding from the veins above the lips helps to cure mouth ulcers, and corrupt gums, and lip cracks, and around the navel.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit before you, and stretch his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	cut then one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the larger one from each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding from the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and with diseases of the uvula, and with diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks under each side to a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then cut one and the other, and do not go too far in depth, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm from which we commonly bleed are bleeding according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or in piercing every one large, or olive-like subtle as arm-cutting, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the bleeding is well-known, and is large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are covered with a thick layer of blood and are apparent, and contain much blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-like bleeding:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is suitable for the surgeon to bleed gently, and to be wary of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great flow of blood comes, then it behooves to stop the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not pierce the bleeding, but cut as with "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open obviously, then it is necessary to extract it, and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Or you want any vein of his, or you open in place of him the vein in the arm: it opens obviously;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut at the inflamed navel, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you open the arm, so that you touch the place until you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the incision and then bind the arm, and cut the vein of the inflamed navel;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: thus escape then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flow upward as urine from a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hasten then, and put your thumb on length, then remove your thumb if the blood stops, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind the arm and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be above fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched, and it beats against you, and the medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a slice of fig skin, and split it, and take one half and bind it well up to the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding stops, it's good; if not, then cure him as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein of the vein in the middle helps as much as it takes blood from the head above and the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that is below, and if he probes too far in, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the wound becomes grievous, and by chance cannot be healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cut the nerves with the instrument from inflamed navel; and escape the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is vein between the two nerves, then cut it along the length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the cephalic helps, which takes blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed in piercing the inflamed olive or inflamed myrtle, for it is the most safe of all veins, for it has no nerve nor artery below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter place, and do not harm anything if it does not take the first time, and one recommences;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the places swell in some men, when one takes the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the vein is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not undertaken except to preserve health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to escape the diseases that are coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are outside: that is to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of prayers in spring, and after eating in autumn and winter, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for diseases has no fixed limit, but when the need arises in day or night, at all hours and in all seasons;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to bleed children until 14 years old, nor a woman who is pregnant except for the last quarter of the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one bleed those who are over 60 years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way it may be, then it is necessary that they purify their bowels with a light clyster;
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not carry away the superfluities from the intestines which are harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one bleed those who are too fat from eating meat, nor those who are drunk, as long as they are thus far gone, nor dropsical people;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware of bleeding after colic passion, and vomiting, and defecation from the belly, and multiple times of having sex with a woman, and labor, watching, and mourning, and all that is contrary to nature, or by something of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then between or bath, if nothing hinders it, to subtlety the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and let the bleeding from the vein of the liver be around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from work, and toil, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be light and joyful, and let the bleeding be higher in that person whom one is bleeding, and rub the arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then loosen the ligament above gently, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and one can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the bleeding spot with a little old oil, then place your thumb of your left hand on that vein below the place where one wants to bleed;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not faint and fail when it is pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings at the time of bleeding, and some that are full of windiness;
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the pressure on the bleeding spot, it withdraws and does not open up the vein, and thus is one of those people;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it overflows the vein, it is too narrow a wound, therefore it is necessary that the bleeder be warned about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein overflows the first time, that is good; but if not, then one recommences slightly below or above the same place in haste, unless the swelling has gone away.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let it remain for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	by chance an abscess will form; do not enter into water, then resume treatment if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly, and you doubt that it will not flow as much blood as you see, then trust in that same opening for all the bleeding right away;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work quickly, however swollen the limb may be; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, do not resume treatment right away, and put on a little bit of lard oil, for it lightens the body's blood, and is nourishing in this swollen limb.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer lard oil to each wound that you treat the veins with, in order to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is done with treacle and vinegar of eyes, when it is put on the limb; so subtly does the blood flow and separate when it becomes too great.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not treated for more than once or twice, or the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hurry, and put on the limb a wet sponge in water and in a little hot oil, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has ceased flowing from the vein, and if there remains on the limb after some days any blackness or greenness, then it does no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on some thing of aloe or myrrh mixed with the juice of camphor, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there appears an abscess and swelling at the wound of the basilica: then put your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft to the pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So be careful that you do not put on any of what we have said, for by chance the artery is cut; but make a dry poultice to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quality and quantity, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become more subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and strong, and has need of bloodletting, that you make a larger wound, and be the bleeding large.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and let it heal slowly and gradually, and one should heal it by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from the cutting off of blood and the tearing of nerves, and is worth more than the healing of the long or broad.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in juice of green apples; if he is heated, then treat the blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, then moisten his bread before the healing in a sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he vomits after the bleeding, then it is necessary that he drink broth of pork and a subtle aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to break his arm and heal again, it is necessary that, when he is weakened by great bleeding, he heals slowly and gradually, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to break his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, then he heals in 72 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another part, then he must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has a great deal of blood within the body that is already heated, and makes him bring on fever; so one must let out a great quantity, and enlarge the opening until it becomes an abscess.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you will follow all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on his pulses when he is healing, so that death does not come in place of abscess.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when the healer is neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it's not necessary when you see that the arm needs to be freed and blood needs to flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly on.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless he is curved, then let him extend his arm quickly, for it would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him heal the second time; or you put at the tip of the bleeding, until the blood that has congealed at the opening of the vein flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on a little bit of oil mixed with water, and press down lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood the second time, then let him bleed in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is healed at the place of the wound because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the blister becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then it is healed now across, not long or broad.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and let it heal well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, then do not put the hand back into hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the salivate of the right hand is worth all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein goes awry, and you cut it all the way through, then nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too far in depth, because the nerves are beneath the skin's layer of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put your hand in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let out as much blood as is necessary, then put oil and salt on the vein to stop it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The pulse on the left hand is indicative of the disease of mouse, and do everything just as I told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The pulse on the forehead is indicative of all diseases that are below the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of urine, and disease of the feet, and groins, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his pulse is that the patient should dip their foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it breaks.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lie above the ankle of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then the pulse indicates either the largest vein or the one at the ankle that is most valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you take the pulse above the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and take the pulse across also as in cutting; and let the flame be anointed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding fails at first, then repeat the second time above a little bit, because the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor fear for nerves, as we have said, and do the same thing on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its pulse indicates the pain of the loins when it's hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its pulse is that the patient should enter or dip into a bath and stretch above the ankle four fingers by twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then let blood in all ways that you can, and crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it's worth more than you cut, for the wound is sound, and it's very well-repaired in many cases.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it, then let blood from any vein that opens or at the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let out as much blood as you see fit, and then release the ligament, and put on cotton and tie it up; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	I assume this is a heading or title for the next section of the text? If so, I'll wait for the translation to continue.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or lead, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping which is not by cutting is done in two ways: either all at once, or step by step;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and cupping which is done by cutting and extracting blood is done in 14 places on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	where one is all around the head, and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on both sides of the neck; and the cup below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cups on the two shoulders; and the cups above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cups in both arms; and the cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cups on both ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, unless from small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one should not be afraid of it, as one is with vein bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it's not fitting that it be administered, neither all at once nor step by step, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of diseases it is necessary to cup, or for customs, then we administer each hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to cup, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who find repletion and inflammation in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and spit up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who see visions, and see through dark blood and hurt and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the midst of the month, we order them to cup after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The pulse of the nose is helpful for the heaviness of the head... that comes to them, and it's not fitting for this to be done after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this cupping is in place of the pulse of the cephalic;
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it's not fitting for someone with a cold complexion or who has cathartic properties, because this would cause them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it's not fitting for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover from it become forgetful, and because of this it's necessary to put the cup a little lower down due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping on the neck is in place of the pulse of the head and the cervical spine, and because of this it's worth it for the constriction of the stomach.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to splitting of the channel of the womb, and to all sorts of pains, and to repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it's necessary to push a little bit, because if it holds too tightly, it will cause forgetfulness or obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The cupping on both sides of the neck is worth for headaches, and obtalmia and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it's in place of the pulse of the cervical spine; and it's necessary that you instruct the patient to stretch their hand when putting it in, so as not to cut the artery and avoid excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The cupping below the chin is worth for mouth diseases, and for corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it's in place of the pulses of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The scapular effusions are worth a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The effusions of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it drains blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply in front, for the flesh is bare of fat, and there are nerves and arteries below.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice that is on the backside is worth as much as hemorrhoids of the fundament, and similar diseases below, and it must be large, and made of earth, so that it can well draw out; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break through; and it would cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The poultices of the legs are manifestly healing, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are worth as much as the old pains of the kidneys, bladder, and womb, and restore the flowers; and they are placed above the two Sophene bones, and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and bring about faintness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the poultice is to put it on first empty, and then suck in a temperate way, and apply it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do so until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood; then stop, and put on new poultices, and take heed of the disposition of the body, for there are some who have thin skin, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike once only, and necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out a little bit of blood at a time, we can only stand one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we often start again; and if the blood is thick, we strike in deep, and the end is that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for one who has thick skin and hard, and those with large pores, that you anoint the places of the poultices with oily and dissolvent balm.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of hellebore, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one being treated has tender skin and large pores, there is no need to put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rise easily with water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or water of succory, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to use a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the poulticing.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be warned when he should be pouticed and when he is being pouticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too abundant and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary that he take cold things, such as green apples and endive and lettuce at ease, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mild poutings, and fatty flesh, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and moderately aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and mild poutings, and small game birds and quail.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be poulticed, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men a little triticale or muscatel wine before the poulticing, or after, in order to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The poultices that are applied without striking are those that are applied on the liver, and on the mussels, and podagra, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the backside, for these members do not tolerate being struck there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done to draw blood from member to member,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as we put on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put poultices on the belly and on the navel to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it relieves pain when there is inflammation or swelling, and it relieves by its attractive power, perhaps the inflammation, or moves the swelling from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the mussels when there is retained flatulence.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these poultices are administered empty to suck for as long as one wishes; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the poultice with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be about two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have a little notch or cavity around the middle, just as one would put an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be made of earth, soft and gentle so that it does not hurt the patient when applied to the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a rod of traversed earth or iron, to put a candle pressed.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be great and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the poultices for children are different from those for old people, and for thin ones from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus apply this poultice to the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle made of wax or a linen thread, and place it inside the poultice across the rod that is inside the poultice,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the bellows so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and have the threads on the valve that we mentioned, so that when one wants to, the steam goes out, and remove the bellows;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the bandage just like before, and reapply it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bellows then that is administered to patients with pleurisy, at all times, there is no rod nor valve, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed on the member just once;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sutures are only applied when there is no place to put bellows because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare bones without flesh, such as the skull or vertebrae, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find sutures that are in sweet and clean water without stirring, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a nut in sweet water until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with wine and bellows, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sutures;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and swollen, if it is a place where one can put bellows, then put them there, because this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the bone slightly, and then in water, very well, and then bind it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bone heals too much after the sutures are applied to the body, soak one cloth of linen in cold water and apply it, until the sutures are tightened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the sutures are multiplied, put on vitriol powder or gall, and similar things, until it is tightened;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put half a handful of peeled beans on the bone, and leave them until they stick to the bone, then it will be tightened now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other sutures.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the sutures will not take hold, rub the bone with fresh blood, or insert a needle and sew until the sutures come out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will stick;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling out, powder on a little bit of alum and silk burnt, or ashes, so they will stick now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins here;
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a treatment for fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish men will fall from this chapter, for they never saw any of the old books nor read a letter;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is strange the science in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing except through the science of old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of instruments that are administered, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say the prologue to this book, summarizing the words and chapters where wise men place their understanding and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, unless something else entirely prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or childhood, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is not very cold or too hot; and I mean by cold, namely, cold joints, and flesh of hare and of goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill oneself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt about aposteme hot, or spreading of matter in the member; then restore the patient to his previous governance which he has used.
