Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meat that makes great nourishment, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and ris, and testicles, and feet, and belly of whale, and eel, and fresh fish, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the patient is restored more quickly and sooner than the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old people and those who are decrepit cannot be well taken up or joined together according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not care, apply a thick paste to the broken bone which sets and joins the member together, so that it strengthens as it was before; and do not leave its work, and therefore it is necessary to nourish with large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is another than the fracture of the chest or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that occurs when an arm is broken, and another in bending, such as the breaking of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also a fracture with wound, and a fracture with a small crack throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own device, and its proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory brings it into place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is known by that which the joint is twisted, and it opens well by pulling apart, and sounds under the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twistiness nor sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, unless there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have a twist, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So do not move it by hand, but put on medications that come later, and then bind it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that occurs in an arm and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary to bind them now equally, so that hot apostemes may not arise.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, let him leave it alone for a day, until the abscess is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it in order with the muscles that you can move lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is more gentle than the restorations of someone who has parts; then restrain it, as is fitting hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and they stretch over two parts, whether it is hands or feet, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two cords, or one cord and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member in its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, then reset by all means the additions to their places with the muscles that you can, and take care that through your work the patient does not suffer injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and fit well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well: then straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring about hot abscess and contraction in the member through their work, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, then instruct the patient well not to move it, whether awake or asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it needs to be put in such a position that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straightly, lest tortuousness come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones; then it is necessary to envelop them in soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are big, such as thighs and leg: then it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and strong linen, because the wide linens encircle all the great member and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind it around with gentle bandages, three turns or four according to the member, and hold your hand for a little on all the linen, then go above the break and restrain it less, so that the break may gradually move away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen little by little, until you take up a great part of the healthy place, then take another linen and turn it around again above the broken joint.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and restrain it moderately, not too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first chapter above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages linen cloths or drapes, so that it is entirely even, then tie all above one bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something calming hot abscess and which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then strain on top of your splints, and be made of half a well-seasoned cane, or of wood from which one makes pegs, or of palm branches, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint you put on top of the break is a little bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also as long as it needs to be for the member, whether small or great.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then strain on top of the splints just as you did in the first chapter, then tie above with a hemp thread, just as in the first chapter above the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is on top, the looser it should be below; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their threads from twisted linen and do wrong, it is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it does not need to have less than two fingers' breadth between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is hurt by the joints of the splints after the straining in their healthy places, then put below them bandages of linen or flaxen cloth, so that he does not get injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the sinew is torn, I will say its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to strain splints on all the broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not necessary to put splints on them except after five days or seven days, or more according to your security about hot abscesses occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the way of ancient poultices to restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that remains at the walls of the mill, and mix it with a great deal of egg, and put this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the poultice restoring the break in several dispositions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of poultice restoring the break and dislocation and torsion: take 20 parts of absinthe and ladani and enule and asefetide and gum arabic and myrrh, 5 parts; aloes, 8 parts; and grind them into powder, and mix with a great deal of egg; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this poultice, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of poultice that is worth for torsion: take mugat and vismalve, 10 parts; mirre and aloes, 8 parts; acaica, 6 parts; Armenian bolic, 10 parts, and grind well, and mix with water or a great deal of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of poultice for joints and bones separated from their places, and soothes the pain that follows, and the use is to cut away the bone and the break: take new linen, and moisten it with a little vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on top of the area. These poultices do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly remove the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to soothe the remaining abscess. Take root of wormseed, chamomile, violet flowers, rice flour, from each one equal part; grind it, mix with wine, and apply to the member that is inflamed, or mix with moist coriander water, or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way to plaster that is stronger than the first one, when abscess persists during the restoration of the member. Take roots of wormseed, and flax seeds, balm, melilotus, and safflower, and violet flowers and chamomile, from each one equal part; grind it, mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hipocrates writes in his book that one should not apply anything to a broken member before restoring it except for a compound made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should apply dry things slightly warm to a broken member in order to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort and human hair or bird feathers and wormseed, and equal parts of all, grind it, and make a plaster and the like.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not loosen it for three days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, with no rest or swelling, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift up the place until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then apply dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is hot.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and the pain be removed, then recommence the gentle binding, and a little plaster, and do not strain it so hard as before; and bind gently until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has fully broken open and is red and painful with swelling, and you need to apply plaster and binding again, then do so again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, then do not loosen it until after three days, or four, or five, or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the breakage is repaired and the approximation to the skin above reaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then apply the restraint more strongly than before, and nourish the flesh as I have said before; and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that no pus can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then arise the member with hot water tea every time you loosen it, and let it be each third day, and relax a little the binding.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, then, cut off the pus from the member, and hasten to do what fools do, who leave the member twisted: that is bad, and it is a painful work, and I see no other thing than to tire oneself out and work properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breakings, and diverse forms, and the causes are destined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breakings that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone removes all the bone down to the sacrum which is below the bone, as does a hammer or a flail; and because of this it is called "hauching" or breaking.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound from these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a packed blow, or a split, or a collarbone break, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent breakage that approaches just below the fascia which is under the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is repaired in the bone as finely as a hair, and it is a small split, and because of this it is called this break "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter downwards, and it becomes loose like what blacksmiths do when they hammer on bellows; then the bone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have or had moist skulls, such as the skull of an infant.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and this happens to all these ways of breaking that small pieces are dislodged as they are, and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of breakings through the subtraction above them, and the inquiry made by probing, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs gently on top, then opens up the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the breakage, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, fever, and the flesh issuing forth and turning red, and other similar things in more or less disposition, then he cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unbearable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, otherwise the skin under the bone will be corrupted, and the accidents that we have said will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the breakage of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut through the broken part in this way: and it is that you take hold of the head of the wounded person, and uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and on the shape of the wound as gently as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if bleeding comes to uncover the bone or abscess appears, then give the aid that is needed, and it is that you should fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed and you are assured of no further bleeding; then begin to remove it around the bone, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you scrape with a narrow tool in front, and it is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another instrument larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various instruments with different shapes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron, and work lightly so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can administer instruments with handles, not too deep or they will go through the bone of the skull, and should have above the point a margin or a circle, so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and you need to have several, each one fitting its own place in the shape of the bone, so that you can have handles for all skulls; and this is the form of the three ways of handles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put a handle on the bone, and turn it to your right until you know the bone has been pierced; then place the handle elsewhere a little bit later, and do this all around, then scrape out the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertuis, and make it as fine as possible, lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have, such as forceps, pincers; and beware not to touch the brain or the sacral membrane.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you take up the applicator which remains of the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more taut and more subtle than the other incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or no scales, then gently loosen them with one of the instruments; then care for the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of work is that which the Gauls say, which is more sound; and he lifts it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is most open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lenticular incisor, which has the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut at one place, and it is the part that is worn away on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly scrape the bone all around, and be well aware of the membrane that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then gently loosen it, because one loosens it very harmlessly and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach to the membrane, and the bone is scraped so only on top, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper which you should have in various quantities, in order to administer in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	And take before great scrapers, and after more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other fine and subtle breakages, it is necessary that you administer according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily understood by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sacral membrane is exposed, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not injure the sacral membrane, then administer above one layer at a time, and do not strain it too much until it holds the wound alone.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for one or two days until the abscess is calmed, then loosen it and administer medicines such as lily roots, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer medicine without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and beware that the wound is thus clean, that you do not leave any ointment or allow it to assemble with bowels, for when bowels assemble above the membrane of the brain, they will flow and burst forth, and bring great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the sacral membrane, it will necrotize above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accidents befall the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if nothing else comes forth except through the medicine that has been placed on it, which has such virtue, it is necessary that you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them with one cloth, and place it on the sacral membrane.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then care for him in ways that are necessary, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only swells or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your small finger or pertuis of the nose, and put equal pressure on that break inside your index finger, and at the back part by pushing forward, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach to the place, it is necessary that you put it equal to the head of a rod, a little big.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do it the same way, and hasten to restore it the next day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is calmed, then insert at the head of the nose threads of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you thrust one thing against another, if there is a break; and let the tents be so large that they fill the holes of the night.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some physicians say that the tents should be moistened with butter, and changed each day. It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary for them to be moistened in the making of an egg yolk, and mill powder; then leave the tent, until the bone is hard, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes it is necessary to put owl's down feathers in place of tents, and if there is a soft wrapping around, and the break is held tight, and blows on the patient; or make what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes forth while you are working on it, then put a poultice or wet cotton in rose oil, or in one pint of aquilion.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not come forth, then put an emplaster by default, of barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put it on light cauterizers, and do not bind the night.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the night is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for this, then sew the gash, and treat the things that are swollen, and solidifying, as emplasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the night, then care for the tents, and put poultices of cloth, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below, and there is no wound to be found, and the break is only so far, and is not split in two, except for the cartilages inside, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part of the jaw, that you put your two index fingers in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left side of the jaw, then put your two index fingers from the right hand, and press the break inside lightly, and set it to the other hand by default, and make equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or fracture, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw a poultice, and put on one double wrapping; and put on the wrapping a great iron band well made, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back to point what has changed; and put a poultice on, of mill powder with egg yolk or barley flour, after you have removed the previous poultice; and put on the poultice a light linen cloth, and if the poultices are dry, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes forth, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, reward no part of the bone that has been removed; but gently remove with suitable instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it by degrees according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, then sew the wound, if it is large, and put on one of those poultices suitable for this, to promote flesh, until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks many times before, near the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two, with fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the break has no wound, that you have two assistants, one of whom holds the assistant that feels the broken forceps; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then set the break to your fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor imperfection.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, put under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or linen, and it should be thick according to your necessity; then stretch and lift the forceps, and strain the sphere to your hand, so that you set the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps out backwards because it comes too far in, then it is necessary that the patient lies comfortably on his hatrail, and puts a mean bolster under his shoulder; and has the assistants lower the shoulder so that the bone of the forceps is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the break to your fingers, and if you find it debris-filled, it is necessary that you split it open; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any impediment, then cut it with one of the incisors you have; but put this instrument under the forceps to guard the syphilis.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should resemble a spoon, and not be rough, and be as wide as it is needed, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, such as the fracture of the wound that you made when you cut the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, then sew the wound, and if the fracture is small, or you doubt there will be a hot abscess, then fill the wound with cloth and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes forth, then soak one cloth in rose oil and vinegar, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone a poultice of mill powder and egg yolk, and put light cauterizers on, and put a sphere under the armpit, if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great band of one palm in width, then put one double wrapping on top of the cauterizers and poultice; then take a fine steel three inches wide and long, and wrap it around that band, so that the head of the band is hanging down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the needle on the breakage, and turn the bandage over the healthy shoulder, and under the sick shoulder; and each time rewind it, and when you see that the ligament holds the breakage correctly, and you clearly see that the needle does not move above the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the ligaments loosen, then hold it back.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient sit on their back, and put one small pillow under the shoulder, to lift the assistant up high; so that it relieves the breakage of the forceps by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie them if bad accidents do not occur, for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the poultice if you see that he needs it, and bind and leave it like that, until he is restored; and it is restored in as little as twenty-eight days, and in less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder breakage
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Not long after the shoulder breaks or becomes loose, and it is not known to be inflamed except by touch; then arrange according to the figure of the breakage, and rewind according to its natural form in all ways you can. Then put on the joint powder from the mill with an abundance of egg white, and light bandages, and put on one double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle needle, a little longer than the shoulder, and if there are hairs under the needle anywhere on the shoulder, use that hair to sew up the stitches so that the needle stays even; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the needle does not move from its place, and check the ligament each day. And every time it relaxes, bind it again, and put the needle back in its place if it has gotten out of joint, and make the patient sit on their side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that sets itself free lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone appears ahead and points below the joint, then go up and cut it, and make what we have said about relieving an abscess to cool.
de la brisure dou pis	of the rib breakage
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The ribs are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but they often break at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, then bend downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks air, and everything, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the hairline on the broken bone, and it seems to be well done.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient sits on their back, and puts one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the edges of the two sides with your hands, and makes it even in all ways you can, so that the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put on poultices and bandages over the subtle needle of salt or another light material, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the ligament back around to the back, and bind it tightly, and reward each hour with oil, and if it relaxes, then bind again; and if it needs to be untied because of corrosion or pruritus that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, and remove the poultice, and address what has come there in ways of cures; then rewind the poultice, and bind until he is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib breakage
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakage of the ribs does not occur except in large places after the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend except because they are slippery; and it seems well to inquiry from above.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the breakage in its place, as it should be. And then put on a poultice, and bind with a needle if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breakage of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, just like a pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and breathes with difficulty, and everything and vomits a great amount of bloody discharge, and this is a grievous illness, and the ancients have put great ingenuity.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the breakage to the end.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless abscesses hot and inflamed come, if it has come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should put cupping glasses on the joint to suck strongly, and this seems like a reason; however, there is doubt whether the cupping glass will attract the superfluities to the joint because of the weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the joint with a moist wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the ligament around, then be cured by the treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone piercing the membrane, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to open up on the broken ribcage, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to ward off the pus; and then one must cut the bone, and pull gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure with poultices until he is healed. And if abscesses come hot, then put on moist cloths in rose oil on the joint; and cure the joint as needed for an abscess, and be careful to sit on the side where it should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the collarbone breakage
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Occasionally comes a breakage of the collarbone, and rarely bends; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you see if he will be healed or not, then take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you press them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that it is mortal in several dispositions, and if they are moved and feel well when one binds and presses them tightly, know that the jointure of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if something like this happens to the spine of the back, and you see if he will be healed or not, then take heed if his feet are softened, and if there is no feeling in his hands, and on his back, there is a great ventosity and egestion without willing; and when one has taken care of his belly, there is a great egestion without willing. And when he is taken care of on his back and he wants to rest, but cannot. Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you rub him if there is a warm abscess, and put oil of rosery or egg yolk on it until it is appeased; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and he should not sleep at all on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are dislocated, it is necessary to cover with a splint; and take the bone away, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if they are large, by stitching, then treat with ointment anointing flesh, until he is healed; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the "joint of the cow", place your pouch on your left hand and hold it equal to your right hand at your power, then apply a plaster and an iron bandage if necessary; then bind it tight, and if there are loose bones, do so again, and remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the breaking of the hipbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the hipbone is broken, and if it does happen, then there follows a little diminishment at the head; and make it long, and decline to the nape of the neck, and comes to the patient with pain at the joint, and puncture, and swells up what has been broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, until you are above the breakage; and know what kind of breakage it is and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the head, then place equal to that breakage, until it is in natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is from the length, or it declines inwardly, then make the patient lie on their belly, until the restoration of that breakage becomes apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it equal, then put on a plaster, and then put on a wooden or horn bandage, and bind the breakage so that it does not move; and apply the joint below the ribs, until the bones are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if warm abscesses come, do not touch them, until the warm abscess is appeased, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as it needs to be bound, if there is no bad accident; and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the breast and the head of the arm, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of the two manners: one of which is that you take one piece of straight wood with a middle groove, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind with two joints, and bend them upwards, and make the patient sit on one seat; then throw his broken arm onto the wood, until it comes to the position, and has about half a wooden curve, then bend down onto some heavy thing or have the minister stretch it downwards; then place the mirror so that the breakage is equal in his hands together, until the breakage returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you support the patient on their hatreil, and bind his hand to his neck, then instruct two ministers to have one hold what is on the breakage in their hands, and the other extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then bind one ligament under the breakage, and on top of the breakage, and have each minister extend to their part. And if the breakage is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary to place one ligament in the middle under the seat, and another towards the breast, under the breakage; and similarly if the breakage is towards the breast, it is necessary to put one ligament lightly, without effort, until the breakage is equal on the joint, and on the breast; then make equal the breakage, as it should be, and bind it, unless warm abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if warm abscesses come, then do not bind it until seven days, and put on a moist linen cloth in oil of rose, until the warm abscess is appeased; then bind it, and the manner of binding is that you put the plaster on the breakage, then bring together the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the bandage, and bind on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in a state of rest, unless some thing hinders it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use iron bands, and put on the breakage a larger and stronger band than the others, with two spaces between each band, and have each band so large that it passes over the breakage three fingers from each side; then bind on the bands, thus as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, more strongly and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the seat of the bands and the binding, as we have said, in the work that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the warm abscess, then leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each three days the band, lest pruritus or inflammation come to the place, or numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tight. If so, address it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and put under the shoulder a pillow made of equal linen, and look at each hour of the day or night to see that the figure of the broken member does not change, or become slackened the bandages; then address it through the power of medicine, and give them food as we have said before, in such a way that the food is for the first subtle ones; and when they begin to recover, let it be thick. And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken up again after forty days altogether; and then one must remove the bandage and administer baths and medicines of ointments to direct the place. And if the stricture is ugly and swollen, one must wait a day or two months before removing the bandage.
de la brisure du bras	I think I have been reading an excerpt from a medieval medical treatise on the treatment of a broken arm (la brisure du bras). The text is written in Old French, and it describes various methods for setting and binding a broken arm, as well as providing instructions for post-operative care.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fasciculus", from which one is small, and it supports the pouch; and the other is great, and it lies below, towards the little toe. By chance, the great fasciculus breaks alone, or the small, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fasciculus is broken, restoration is easy, and healing; and when the great one is broken, so is healing poor, and more grievous than when both are broken together. If it is the small fasciculus that is broken alone, then you must slightly extend it and make it equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the great fasciculus, then you must stretch it more strongly; and extend it on one cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the other, and the small toes lower than the other toes, so that the patient crosses over himself, with one cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the minister's arm to the part below his hand, or to a strap, and another minister to another above. And then place it so that it is equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then place each in its place, and if there are any that are loosened or protrude, and you cannot restore them to their place, then fashion them with a saw and an osteum, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it has an open wound from the breaking, I spoke of it in the singular chapter; then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration a boil arises, then apply one cloth made from rose ointment and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth gently over the boil until it is pacified. And then remove the ointment and put on an embalming powder with a lot of eggwhite; then put in candles, and let the candle at the breakage be a bit stronger and slightly wider than the others; and know that it should have 7 candles or arms in multiple dispositions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two; and bind more tightly over the breakage than other parts, and always less as you go along, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter. And let the cloths that are on the breakage be soft and moist, not hard or dry; and let the son-in-law, who is being bound, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the strap after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident happens to the member, such as pruritus that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member in hot water until those pruritus are pacified; and let the member rest not too tightly. And then resume binding, and if the strap is worn out and the bone loosened, and similar things, then address them.
